Repetition of Permission in a Conditional Oath
Deriving the ruling that permission must be repeated in 'except with my permission' oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the ruling that permission must be repeated in an oath with 'except with my permission' using the Hanafi analysis of istithna mufarrag.

Core Idea
An istithna mufarrag requires permission for each instance because no exception is made without it.

In this lesson, we explore a detailed derivation (istinbat) from a common oath scenario: 'If you go out except with my permission, you are divorced.' The Hanafi scholars analyze the linguistic structure to determine how many permissions are needed. The key lies in identifying the exception as mufarrag (disconnected), which attaches the exception clause to every potential act. This contrasts with similar Quranic expressions, where a different structure allows a single permission. By the end, you will be able to apply this reasoning to analogous cases in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Exception Type
Examine the phrase 'إلا بإذني'. Determine if it is an istithna mufarrag (disconnected exception) by checking if the general term is omitted. Here, the implicit general term 'خروج' is omitted, making it mufarrag.
Hanafi usul: an istithna mufarrag binds the exception to each individual of the genus.
2
Analyze the Grammatical Attachment
The preposition 'ب' requires a related verb. The implicit verb is 'خروج' (going out). Thus the meaning becomes: 'a going out attached to permission'. Only such goings-out are excluded from the prohibition.
The attachment (ta'alluq) is crucial: the exception modifies each going-out.
3
Derive the Ruling
Since all goings-out are prohibited except those attached to permission, each separate going-out requires its own permission. One permission does not cover all future goings-out.
This yields a ruling different from the Quranic verse about entering the Prophet's houses, which uses 'إلا أن يؤذن' (except when you are permitted).
4
Contrast with a Similar Wording
Compare with 'إن خرجت إلا أن آذن' (if you go out except that I permit). Here 'إلا أن' makes the permission a ghaya (limit), not an exception. One permission suffices until revoked.
The difference hinges on the syntactic role of the permission phrase.
5
Address the Quranic Objection
The text anticipates an objection from verse 33:53. The Hanafi response: repetition of permission there is due to the 'illa (cause) of harming the Prophet, not the wording. In the oath, no such illa exists, so the wording governs.
This illustrates the principle that ruling can shift based on underlying cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع. يلزم للبر (تكرار الإذن في : إن خرجت إلا بإذني فأنت طالق (لأنه) استثناء (مفرغ) لأن الباء لا بد لها من متعلق، وذلك هو الخروج، فالمعنى : إن خرجت بأي خروج كان إلا خروجاً ملصقاً بإذني فلم يخرج من المنع خروج (خارج إلا ملصقاً به) أي بالإذن، والخروجات الغير الملصقة بالإذن ممنوعة داخلة تحت اليمين فيشترط الإذن لكل خروج بخلاف إن خرجت (إلا) أن آذن لأن الإذن غاية تجوزاً وليس باستثناء والمعنى إن خرجت إلى الإذن به لتعذر الاستثناء) لعدم دخول الإذن تحت الخروج، وإذا كان غاية فيتحقق البرّ بالمرة الواحدة من الإذن لعدم تحقق الشرط وهو الخروج قبل الإذن، فإن قلت : فمن أين لزم تكرار الإذن في دخول بيوت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع أنه قال الله تعالى: لَا نَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتَ النَّبِيِّ إِلَّا أَن يُؤذن لكم ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٣] قال : (ولزوم تكرار الإذن في دخول بيوته عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام إنما هو بالتعليل) وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ ذَلِكُمْ كَانَ يُؤْذِي النَّبِيَّ وإيذاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حرام في كل وقت لا بلفظ النهي أقول حذف حرف الجر ههنا) أي مع أن (قياس) فلم لا يقدر، ويصير الأصل إلا بأن آذن فيصير مثل إلا بإذني والمصدر) استعماله (للحين) أيضاً (شائع) كثير فلم لا يجوز أن يكون للحين والمعنى إلا وقت أن آذن الاستثناء فيصح عموم الأوقات، وعلى هذين الوجهين يلزم تكرار الإذن في كل مرة (فما وجه الترجيح) لما
Branch. It is necessary for fulfillment (al-birr) to repeat permission in: 'If you go out except with my permission, you are divorced.' Because it is an exceptive (istiṯnā’) that is mufarrag (disconnected), since the باء must have an attachment, and that is the going out. So the meaning is: 'If you go out with any going out except a going out attached to my permission.' So no going out is excluded from the prohibition except one attached to it (i.e., permission). Goings-out not attached to permission are prohibited, included in the oath, so permission is required for each going out. Unlike 'if you go out except that I permit,' because permission is a limit (ghāya) metaphorically, not an exception. The meaning is: 'If you go out up to the permission,' because the exception is impossible due to permission not being included under going out. Since it is a limit, birr is achieved by one instance of permission because the condition (going out) does not occur before permission. If you say: Whence does the repetition of permission become necessary in entering the houses of the Prophet ﷺ when Allah said: 'Do not enter the houses of the Prophet except when you are permitted' [al-Aḥzāb 53]? He said: 'The repetition of permission in entering his houses ﷺ and his Companions is due to the legal cause (ta‘līl),' which is His saying: 'Indeed, that used to harm the Prophet' and harming the Prophet is forbidden at all times, not by the wording of prohibition. I say: The deletion of the preposition is here, i.e., despite that, the analogy – so why is it not estimated, and the original becomes 'except with permission,' making it like 'except with my permission'? And the masdar is also commonly used for the moment (al-ḥīn). So why may it not be for the moment, meaning 'except the time I permit,' so the exception applies and the generality of times holds? On these two aspects, repetition of permission is necessary each time. So what is the basis for preference?
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage performs an istinbat (derivation) on the ruling for an oath like 'إن خرجت إلا بإذني فأنت طالق' (If you go out except with my permission, you are divorced). The key is that the استثناء (exception) is مفرغ (disconnected), meaning the exception phrase is not preceded by a general statement. Because the باء requires a relation (تَعَلُّق), the meaning becomes: 'If you go out with any going out except a going out attached to my permission.' Thus, any going out not with permission is prohibited, so each separate going out needs its own permission. The text contrasts this with 'إن خرجت إلا أن آذن' (if you go out except that I permit), where permission is a غاية (limit) and one permission suffices. The author then addresses a potential objection from the Quranic verse about entering the Prophet's houses, explaining that the repetition there is due to the harm (علة), not the wording. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing further possible analyses (like estimating the preposition or interpreting المصدر as لحين) and asks for the basis of preference, indicating a scholarly discussion. This shows detailed Hanafi usul analysis.

Key Terms
استثناء مفرغ (istiṯnā’ mufarrag): An exception where the general term is omitted; it affects the ruling by requiring the exception clause to attach to every instance.
البر (al-birr): Fulfillment of the oath; here it means avoiding the conditional divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analysis of 'إن خرجت إلا بإذني فأنت طالق', why must permission be repeated for each going out?
A) Because the word 'إلا' indicates generality
B) Because the exception is mufarrag and attaches to each act
C) Because the oath is conditional on each exit
D) Because the husband's permission expires after one use

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an istithna mufarrag requires repetition of the exception clause for each instance, unless a specific 'illa overrides.

The Difference Between 'غداً' and 'في غد' in Divorce Statements
Explaining the effect of intention and the difference between 'غداً' and 'في غد'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of apparent meaning (zahir) to distinguish between the judicial and religious acceptance of intention in time-specified divorce statements.

Core Idea
The presence or absence of 'في' determines whether the husband’s intention to defer divorce is accepted judicially.

This passage examines a subtle linguistic distinction in divorce pronouncements. The Hanafi school holds that the statement 'You are divorced tomorrow' (without 'في') implies divorce at the first moment of the day, while 'in tomorrow' (with 'في') does not imply immediate coverage. This has significant practical consequences for judicial rulings versus religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two statements and their apparent meanings
Locate the phrases 'أنت طالق غداً' and 'في غد' in the source. Note that 'غداً' without 'في' signals full coverage (isti‘āb) of the day, while 'في غد' does not.
The particle 'في' restricts the coverage to a part of the day.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa’s position on intention
Abu Hanifa holds that without 'في', the husband’s intention to defer divorce to the end of the day is not accepted judicially because it contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir). The divorce occurs at the first moment of tomorrow.
This is based on the principle that the apparent meaning governs in judicial matters.
3
Compare with the Sahibayn’s position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the husband’s intention even without 'في'. They prioritize the husband’s actual intent over the apparent linguistic implication.
The dispute reflects a deeper usul difference regarding the role of intention versus apparent meaning.
4
Distinguish between judicial (qadā’) and religious (diyāna)
Judicially, the apparent meaning prevails. Religiously, the husband’s intention is accepted in both statements, meaning he is not sinful if his intention matches his inner state.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh, balancing legal certainty and personal accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويخالف هذا (خلافاً لهما، فلم يصدق قضاء) عنده (في نية آخر النهار في قوله : أنت طالق غداً لأنه نوى خلاف حقيقته الظاهرة، وفيه تخفيف، فإنه يفيد استيعاب إنصاف المرأة بالطلاق تمام الغد، وذلك بالوقوع في أول أجزائه (بخلاف في غد فإنه يقبل فيه نية آخر النهار لعدم اقتضائه الاستيعاب، فإن قلت: فلم قلتم بوقوعه في أول الأجزاء عند عدم النية ؟ قال : (وإنما يتعين أوّل الغد مع عدم النية لعدم المزاحم هناك، بخلاف الأجزاء الباقية، فإن الأول مزاحم لها، فالوقوع فيها دونه رجحان من غير مرجح فافهم. هذا حكم القضاء، وأما ديانة فيقبل نية آخر النهار في الصورتين
And this differs (contrary to the two companions [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]), so he did not accept judicially (according to him) the intention of the end of the day in his statement: 'You are divorced tomorrow' because he intended contrary to its apparent reality, and there is leniency in it, for it (the statement without 'fī') indicates covering the woman with divorce throughout the whole of tomorrow, and that is by occurring at its first part. (Contrary to 'in tomorrow', for in that case the intention of the end of the day is accepted because it does not imply coverage. If you say: Why do you say it occurs at the first part when there is no intention? He said: The first of tomorrow is determined when there is no intention due to the absence of a competing part; unlike the remaining parts, for the first competes with them, so occurrence in them without it would be a preference without a preferred. Reflect. This is the judicial ruling; as for religiously, the intention of the end of the day is accepted in both cases.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage discusses the difference between saying 'You are divorced tomorrow' (without 'fī') and 'in tomorrow' (with 'fī'). Without 'fī', the apparent meaning is that the divorce occurs at the beginning of tomorrow, covering the entire day. The husband's intention to defer to the end of the day is not accepted judicially (qadā'), because it contradicts the apparent meaning and would involve leniency. With 'fī', the apparent meaning does not imply full coverage, so the intention of the end of the day is accepted. The Hanafi position is that without 'fī', the divorce takes effect at the first part of the designated day because it is the only part that is certain; later parts would be speculative. Religiously (diyānatan), the husband's intention is accepted in both cases.

Key Terms
قضاء (qadā’): Judicial ruling based on apparent evidence, not on internal intentions.
استيعاب (isti‘āb): Full coverage; the linguistic implication that 'غداً' without 'في' covers the entire day.
ظاهر (zāhir): Apparent meaning of a statement, as understood by common usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the judicial ruling when a husband says 'You are divorced tomorrow' (without 'في') and intends the end of the day?
A) The divorce occurs at the end of the day as intended.
B) The divorce occurs at the beginning of the day.
C) The divorce is invalid because of conflict between intention and statement.
D) The judge must reconcile both views.

Key Takeaway
The presence of 'في' changes the judicial treatment of intention in time-specified divorce statements, but religiously intention is always accepted.

The Effect of 'Mashī’a' vs. '‘Ilm' in Conditional Divorce
Explaining why divorce does not occur with 'mashī’a' but does with '‘ilm'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats 'in God's will' as a conditional phrase that suspends divorce, while 'in God's knowledge' causes immediate divorce, and apply this linguistic distinction to similar statements.

Core Idea
Mashī’a triggers a condition; ‘ilm affirms actuality — one suspends, the other executes.

In this passage, the author tackles a subtle linguistic question: when a husband attaches his divorce pronouncement to God's attributes, does the divorce take effect? The answer hinges on how each attribute functions in common legal language. 'Will' (mashī’a) is conventionally understood as a conditional — 'if God wills' — while 'knowledge' (‘ilm) points to actual reality. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, showing how urf (customary usage) and linguistic nuance shape legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three phrases
The passage examines three expressions: 'in the will of God', 'in the power of God', and 'in the knowledge of God'. List them.
2
Analyze the default understanding of each
For mashī’a, the immediate understanding (mubtadir) is conditional. For qudra, it could be either decree (like mashī’a) or capacity (like potential). For 'ilm, it is knowledge of actual existents.
3
Read the objections and responses
The text includes objections: e.g., God's will is necessarily existent so divorce should occur. The Hanafi response: the linguistic convention overrides theological necessity.
4
Extract the Hanafi principle
The principle: when a statement can be interpreted as a condition (due to urf), it suspends the ruling; when it affirms actuality, the ruling is immediate.
5
Apply to the three cases
Mashī’a: conditional → no immediate effect. Qudra: ambiguous → no immediate effect. ‘Ilm: actual → immediate effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع. قالوا لو قال : أنت طالق في مشيئة الله تعالى يتعلق بها، ولا يقع، لأن المشيئة غير معلومة بخلاف طالق في علم الله لأنه إنما يتعلق بموجود فنوقض بطالق في قدرة الله، فأجيب بأن المعنى في تقدير الله فهو كفى مشيئة الله فلا يقع، ورد بأنه يجوز أن يكون المعنى في مقدور الله تعالى ومقدوره متحقق فينبغي أن يقع والمصنف قرر الكلام، هذا بحيث لا يتأتى هذا القيل والقال فقال (لم يقع في قوله طالق) في مشيئة الله و) قوله : طالق (في قدرة الله لصحة تعلقهما بطرفي (النقيضين فلا يتعين فيه الوقوع، وهذا غير ظاهر في المشيئة، فإن المشيء الله تعالى واقع بالضرورة، فالأولى أن يقرر هكذا أن المتبادر من الشرط وهو يستقيم في المشيئة فالمعنى إن شاء الله ،فطالق والشرط غير معلوم الوقوع، وفي القدرة لا يستقيم الاشتراط في الظاهر فإما أن يعني به إن قدر الله كما إذا كان القدرة التقدير، فهو كإن شاء الله تعالى، وإما أن يعني في مقدور الله تعالى فلا معنى له، إلا أن بمعنى في جملة مقدوراته والموجود والمعدوم كلاهما مقدوران فلا يتعين الوجود والوقوع، وهذا (بخلاف) طالق (في علم الله تعالى فإنه يقع فيه في الحال لأنه لا يتعلق إلا بالواقع المحقق فيجب أن يتحقق الطلاق فتدبر)
Branch: They said: If he says: 'You are divorced in the will of God Almighty', it is suspended and does not occur, because the will is unknown. Unlike 'divorced in the knowledge of God', because it is only connected to an existent. Then it was objected with 'divorced in the power of God'. So it was answered that the meaning is 'in the decree of God' so it is like 'in the will of God' and does not occur. And it was refuted that it could mean 'in the power of God Almighty' and His power is real, so it should occur. The author settled the discussion in a way that does not allow these objections: He said: (It does not occur in his statement 'divorced') in the will of God and (his statement) 'divorced' (in the power of God) because it is valid to relate them to both extremes of the opposites, so occurrence is not determined. But this is not apparent in the case of will, for the will of God is necessarily existent. So it is better to explain as follows: the immediate understanding is condition, which is sound with will; so the meaning is 'if God wills', and the condition is unknown of occurrence. Regarding power, a condition is not sound outwardly; so either it means 'if God decrees' as if power is decree, then it is like 'if God wills'; or it means 'in the power of God' which has no meaning except 'in the totality of His powers', and existent and non-existent are both within His power, so existence and occurrence are not determined. This is contrary to 'divorced in the knowledge of God Almighty', for it occurs immediately because it is only connected to a real occurrence, so divorce must be realized. So reflect.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage resolves a dispute about divorce statements tied to God's attributes. If a man says 'You are divorced in the will of God', the immediate understanding is a condition (if God wills), and since we do not know if His will is for divorce, it does not occur. The same applies to 'power of God' because it could mean either His decree or His capacity, both of which do not necessitate occurrence. However, 'in the knowledge of God' differs: knowledge is of actual things, so if the statement is true, the divorce must have already occurred. Thus, divorce takes effect immediately. The Hanafi position is that only the last phrase ('in God's knowledge') results in immediate divorce.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashī’a): Will; here it is understood as a conditional expression, not as an attribute of God that necessitates occurrence.
قدرة (qudra): Power; ambiguous between 'decree' (which is like will) and 'capacity' (which includes both possible and actual).
علم (‘ilm): Knowledge; only relates to actual existents, so when attributed to God in divorce context, it affirms the occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does divorce not occur when the husband says 'You are divorced in the will of God'?
A) Because God's will is unknown to humans.
B) Because the phrase is linguistically understood as a condition ('if God wills'), which is uncertain.
C) Because the divorce is invalid in the Hanafi school.
D) Because the husband must explicitly state 'I divorce you'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between attributes that imply conditionality (mashī’a, qudra) and those that affirm actuality (ilm), relying on urf to determine legal effect.

Ghayr as Adjective or Exception in Acknowledgments
Linguistic analysis of 'ghayr' affecting liability in acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether 'ghayr' functions as an adjective or exception based on grammatical case, and apply the Hanafi dispute to determine liability in acknowledgments.

Core Idea
Ghayr's grammatical case determines legal liability: adjective (full) vs exception (remainder), with intra-Hanafi dispute on homogeneity for connectedness.

The word 'ghayr' (other than) in acknowledgments can either describe the item or exclude a part. Its function hinges on grammatical case and the type of homogeneity required for a valid exception. This lesson unpacks the linguistic analysis and the Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn on whether formal or semantic homogeneity suffices, especially for prices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Grammatical Case
Examine the ending of 'ghayr' in the acknowledgment. Nominative (marfu') indicates an adjective; accusative (mansub) indicates an exception.
The original Arabic text uses vowel endings to distinguish: damma vs fatha.
2
Determine Legal Function
If adjective, the acknowledgment covers the entire item. If exception, the acknowledged amount is reduced by the excepted part.
This is the base rule for homogeneous items (e.g., dirham and daniq).
3
Check Homogeneity for Exception Connectedness
For an exception to be connected (muttasil), the excepted item must be homogeneous with the excepted-from. Two views: Imam Muhammad requires homogeneity in form and meaning; the Sahibayn accept semantic homogeneity (e.g., both being prices). If disconnected, exception is void and full liability remains.
The dispute arises when items are of different types, like dinar and dirhams.
4
Apply the Ikhtilaf
In the case 'I owe you a dinar except ten dirhams', Imam Muhammad rules the full dinar binding; the Sahibayn rule the remainder after deducting the value of ten dirhams in gold.
The Sahibayn rely on custom ('urf) in prices for semantic homogeneity.
5
Derive the Ruling
Based on the applicable view, state the amount owed. The text does not choose a tarjih, but later Hanafi practice may follow the Sahibayn due to custom.
This shows how linguistic analysis directly affects legal outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : : (غير متوغل في الإبهام جاء صفة) مضافة على الأصل فيه فلا حكم في المضاف إليه اللهم إلا عند قائلي المفهوم (و) جاء (استثناء، فيفيد نقيض الحكم) فيما بعده، شأن الاستثناء ويلزمه حينئذ إعراب (المستثنى لأن المستثنى لما صار مجروراً بها، هو أجرى إعرابه عليها لكونها صالحة للإعراب ففي له درهم غير دانق بالرفع) صفة درهم (يلزم) الدرهم (تاماً) لأنه إقرار بالدرهم التام المغاير للدائق (و) في له علي درهم غير دائق بالنصب يلزم الدرهم (إلا) دانقاً) لأن الاستثناء تكلم بالباقي، فاقتصر الإقرار على ما بقي من الدرهم بعد إسقاط الدائق (وفي) له دينار) غير عشرة دراهم بالنصب كذلك عندهما فيلزم الباقي من الدينار بعد إخراج قيمة عشرة دراهم من الذهب (و) يلزم دينار (نام عند الإمام (محمد، لأنه) استثناء (منقطع) غير مخرج لشيء عنده لشرطه في الاتصال التجانس بين المستثنى والمستثنى منه (صورة ومعنى) وهو منتف في الدينار والدرهم وإذا لم يخرج شيء يلزم تام (وقالا بكفايته) أي كفاية التجانس (معنى) للاتصال (وهو متحقق) ههنا لاشتراك) (الثمنية بينهما، فالمعنى: له عليَّ دينار إلا قيمة عشرة دراهم من الذهب، وإنما اكتفيا بالتجانس المعنوي في الأثمان فقط وجود المعنوي في له عليّ ألف إلا هذا العبد لأن الأثمان لكثرة الاستعمال وقع فيه هذا العرف دون غيره، ويقال في مثل هذا عند إرادة الاستثناء له على ألف إلا قيمة العبد، ولا يقدر هذا والله أعلم بأحكامه .
Issue: (The word 'ghayr' (other than) not deeply immersed in ambiguity comes as an adjective) as an annexation originally, so there is no ruling on the annexed except according to those who uphold the concept [of mafhum]. (And) it comes as an exception, then it conveys the opposite ruling in what follows, as is the nature of exception, and then it necessitates the grammatical case of the excepted. Because the excepted, when it becomes genitive by it, it runs its case on it due to its suitability for case endings. So in 'he has a dirham other than a daniq' with nominative, it is an adjective of dirham, so the entire dirham is binding, because it is an acknowledgment of the complete dirham distinct from the daniq. And in 'he owes me a dirham other than a daniq' with accusative, the dirham except a daniq is binding, because exception is speaking of the remainder, so the acknowledgment is limited to what remains of the dirham after dropping the daniq. And in 'he has a dinar other than ten dirhams' with accusative, similarly according to [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], so the remainder of the dinar is binding after deducting the value of ten dirhams in gold. And according to Imam Muhammad, a full dinar is binding, because it is a disconnected exception, not removing anything in his view due to his condition for connection: homogeneity between the excepted and excepted-from in form and meaning, which is absent in dinar and dirham. And if nothing is removed, the full [dinar] is binding. And they two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: sufficiency of homogeneity in meaning for connection, and it is realized here due to the commonality of being a price (thimaniyya) between them. So the meaning is: he owes me a dinar except the value of ten dirhams in gold. And they sufficed with semantic homogeneity only in prices, [unlike] the existence of semantic [homogeneity] in 'he owes me a thousand except this slave' because due to frequent usage, this custom occurred for prices and not for others. And it is said in such cases when intending exception: 'he owes me a thousand except the value of the slave', and this is not estimated. And Allah knows best His rulings.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal implications of the word 'ghayr' (غير) when used in acknowledgments (iqrar). It can function grammatically as an adjective (sifa) or as an exception (istithna'). When used as an adjective, the acknowledgment includes the entire item (e.g., 'a full dirham' if said with nominative). When used as an exception (with accusative), the acknowledgment is limited to the remainder after excluding the specified item. A key dispute arises when the items are not of the same genus (e.g., a dinar and dirhams). Imam Muhammad considers such exception disconnected (munqati') because he requires homogeneity in form and meaning, so the exception is void and the full dinar is binding. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) consider semantic homogeneity sufficient (both being prices) and thus treat it as a connected exception, so only the remainder is binding. This applies only to prices due to custom ('urf).

Key Terms
غير (ghayr): A word meaning 'other than'; can be used as adjective (sifa) or exception (istithna') depending on grammatical case.
استثناء منقطع (istithna' munqati'): A disconnected exception where the excepted is not of the same kind as the excepted-from; it is void in Hanafi view.
ثمنية (thimaniyya): The quality of being a price (thaman); gold and silver share this, allowing semantic homogeneity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if someone acknowledges 'I owe you a dinar except ten dirhams' (with 'ghayr' in accusative), what is the ruling?
A) He owes the remainder after deducting the value of ten dirhams
B) He owes the full dinar
C) He owes nothing
D) He owes ten dirhams

Key Takeaway
The grammatical case of 'ghayr' determines liability, but the homogeneity requirement for a valid exception splits the Hanafi school, with custom tipping the scale for prices.

No Synonymy Between Emphasis and Emphasized Words
Definition of taraduf applied to mu'akkad and mu'akkad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two reasons why verbal and moral emphasis do not create synonymy between the emphasized word and the emphasis word.

Core Idea
Synonymy requires different wording and same meaning; emphasis either repeats the word or changes meaning.

In Arabic, emphasis (tawkid) is used to reinforce a statement. But does using a different word for emphasis create a synonym? The Hanafi usul scholars clarify that no, the emphasis word is not a synonym of the emphasized. This lesson unpacks why, both for verbal emphasis (repetition) and moral emphasis (using words like 'nafs'). Understanding this distinction prevents confusion when analyzing texts in fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of emphasis
Recognize that tawkid is divided into lafzi (verbal) and ma'nawi (moral). Verbal emphasis repeats the same word; moral emphasis uses specific emphatic words like nafs, ayn, kull.
2
State the definition of synonymy (taraduf)
Synonymy is defined as two different words having the same meaning. It requires ikhtilaf fi al-lafz (difference in wording) and ittihad fi al-ma'na (unity in meaning).
This is the standard usul definition.
3
Apply to verbal emphasis
In verbal emphasis, the same word is repeated. Since synonymy requires different words, it automatically fails.
Example: 'jā'a jā'a' – both words are identical.
4
Apply to moral emphasis
In moral emphasis, the emphasis word (e.g., 'nafs') carries additional meaning (selfhood), so the meanings are not identical. Thus, synonymy fails again.
The emphasized word and 'nafs' are not synonyms because 'nafs' adds the meaning of self.
5
Conclude the rule
Therefore, there is no synonymy between the mu'akkad (emphasized) and the mu'akkad (emphasis word) in either type of emphasis.
This ruling applies across all Arabic texts in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
لا ترادف بين المؤكد والمؤكد لاتحاد اللفظ كما في التأكيد اللفظي (أو تغاير المعنى) كما في التأكيد المعنوي ولا بد في الترادف من التخالف في اللفظ والاتحاد في المعنى (ولا) ترادف (بين التابع والمتبوع نحو حسن بسن لأنه لو أفرد) عن المتبوع (لا يدل على شيء ولو كان المعنى المفهوم حال التركيب معه مستقلاً بالمفهومية) كيف لا وليس معناه إلا معنى المتبوع فلا يلزم كونه حرفاً كما في «التحرير» وإنما لا يدل التابع (منفرداً) عن متبوعه (لأنه) إنما (وضع) وقرر في الاستعمال التقوية متبوع قبله على زنته فهو) مستعملاً (بدونه مهمل) لا يدل على شيء أصلاً وأما معه وإن دل على معنى لكن ليست دلالته وضعية، بل دلالته كدلالة المقلوبات، وبهذا ظهر لك سر عدم الترادف بينهما، وأما ما ذكره المصنف ففيه خفاء، فإن الدلالة حين الإفراد غير مشروطة في الترادف ألا ترى أن الضمير المتصل والمنفصل مترادفان أنه لا يدل المتصل لو أفرد على شيء أصلاً، وقد يكون الترادف في أصل الحروف أيضاً مع أنه لا دلالة لها حال الإفراد فتدبر .
Issue: There is no synonymy between the emphasized and the emphasis word, due to the unity of the word, as in verbal emphasis, or the difference of meaning, as in moral emphasis. And synonymy requires difference in wording and unity in meaning. And there is no synonymy between the follower and the followed, such as 'hasan basan', because if it is separated from the followed, it does not indicate anything, even if the meaning understood in composition is independent in terms of intelligibility. How not? For its meaning is only the meaning of the followed, so it does not necessitate being a particle, as in 'al-Tahrir'. Rather the follower does not indicate when isolated from its followed because it was established in usage for reinforcement of a preceding followed word of its meter, so it is, when used without it, neglected, indicating nothing at all. As for with it, although it indicates a meaning, its indication is not conventional, but rather its indication is like the indication of inverted words. And by this, the secret of the lack of synonymy between them appears to you. As for what the author mentioned, there is obscurity in it, for indication when isolated is not a condition in synonymy; do you not see that the attached pronoun and the detached pronoun are synonyms, and the attached pronoun if isolated indicates nothing at all? And synonymy may even occur in the original letters, although they have no indication when isolated. So reflect.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition lesson explaining that there is no synonymy between the emphasized word (mu'akkad) and the emphasis word (mu'akkad) itself. In verbal emphasis (like repeating a word), the words are identical, so synonymy requires different words. In moral emphasis (like using 'nafs' or 'ayn'), the meaning differs. Synonymy requires different words and same meaning. The lesson also discusses cases like 'hasan basan' where the follower (basan) only gains meaning from the followed (hasan) and is meaningless alone. However, the author notes that isolation is not a strict condition for synonymy, citing attached and detached pronouns as examples of synonyms where the attached pronoun is meaningless alone. This is a nuanced point: the follower in 'hasan basan' is not a synonym because its meaning is not independent; it only reinforces the followed. The author engages with a potential objection from 'al-Tahrir', clarifying that the follower's function is reinforcement, not independent meaning. The study of such pairs is important for understanding linguistic principles in usul.

Key Terms
التأكيد اللفظي (al-takīd al-lafẓī): Verbal emphasis: repeating the same word for emphasis, e.g., 'jā'a jā'a' (he came, he came).
التأكيد المعنوي (al-takīd al-ma'nawī): Moral emphasis: using words like 'nafs' (self) or 'ayn' (eye) to emphasize the subject, e.g., 'jā'a Zaydun nafsuhu' (Zayd himself came).
الترادف (al-tarāduf): Synonymy: two different words having the same meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is there no synonymy in verbal emphasis?
A) Because the words are the same.
B) Because the meaning changes.
C) Because it is not a pair of words.
D) Because it is not permitted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, synonymy requires both different words and identical meaning; emphasis types fail one of these conditions, so no synonymy exists between mu'akkad and mu'akkad.

No Synonymy Between Follower and Followed
Definition of taraduf applied to tabi' and matbu', with nuance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the follower in a rhyming pair like 'hasan basan' is not a synonym of the followed, and evaluate the author's nuance regarding attached pronouns.

Core Idea
A follower word like 'basan' depends on its followed for meaning; it has no independent signification, so it cannot be a synonym.

In Arabic, some words appear together for reinforcement, like 'hasan basan'. At first glance, 'basan' might seem to mean the same as 'hasan', but Hanafi usul scholars argue it is not a synonym. This lesson examines why, based on the nature of the follower's dependence on the followed. It also addresses a subtle point: the condition of isolation is not strictly required for synonymy, as demonstrated by attached and detached pronouns.

Guided Path
1
Define the follower (tābi') and followed (matbū')
The tābi' is a word that follows another word for reinforcement, e.g., 'basan' in 'hasan basan'. It has no independent meaning; it only reinforces the followed.
2
Identify the condition for synonymy
Recall that synonymy requires different words and same meaning. The follower fails because its meaning is not independent; it is only the meaning of the followed, but its usage is restricted to reinforcement.
The text mentions that if separated, it indicates nothing.
3
Understand the nature of the follower's indication
When paired, the follower indicates the meaning but not through convention (wad') but rather like inverted words (maqlūbāt). Its signification is derived from the followed.
This is why it is not considered a synonym.
4
Consider the author's nuance about isolation
The author points out that lack of indication when isolated is not a condition for synonymy, as attached pronouns (damīr muttaṣil) are synonyms of detached pronouns even though the attached pronoun has no meaning when isolated.
This nuance shows that the follower's case is special due to its purpose of reinforcement.
5
Conclude the rule
Therefore, the follower is not a synonym of the followed because its meaning is not established independently and its role is purely emphatic.
This applies to all such pairs in Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
لا ترادف بين المؤكد والمؤكد لاتحاد اللفظ كما في التأكيد اللفظي (أو تغاير المعنى) كما في التأكيد المعنوي ولا بد في الترادف من التخالف في اللفظ والاتحاد في المعنى (ولا) ترادف (بين التابع والمتبوع نحو حسن بسن لأنه لو أفرد) عن المتبوع (لا يدل على شيء ولو كان المعنى المفهوم حال التركيب معه مستقلاً بالمفهومية) كيف لا وليس معناه إلا معنى المتبوع فلا يلزم كونه حرفاً كما في «التحرير» وإنما لا يدل التابع (منفرداً) عن متبوعه (لأنه) إنما (وضع) وقرر في الاستعمال التقوية متبوع قبله على زنته فهو) مستعملاً (بدونه مهمل) لا يدل على شيء أصلاً وأما معه وإن دل على معنى لكن ليست دلالته وضعية، بل دلالته كدلالة المقلوبات، وبهذا ظهر لك سر عدم الترادف بينهما، وأما ما ذكره المصنف ففيه خفاء، فإن الدلالة حين الإفراد غير مشروطة في الترادف ألا ترى أن الضمير المتصل والمنفصل مترادفان أنه لا يدل المتصل لو أفرد على شيء أصلاً، وقد يكون الترادف في أصل الحروف أيضاً مع أنه لا دلالة لها حال الإفراد فتدبر .
Issue: There is no synonymy between the emphasized and the emphasis word, due to the unity of the word, as in verbal emphasis, or the difference of meaning, as in moral emphasis. And synonymy requires difference in wording and unity in meaning. And there is no synonymy between the follower and the followed, such as 'hasan basan', because if it is separated from the followed, it does not indicate anything, even if the meaning understood in composition is independent in terms of intelligibility. How not? For its meaning is only the meaning of the followed, so it does not necessitate being a particle, as in 'al-Tahrir'. Rather the follower does not indicate when isolated from its followed because it was established in usage for reinforcement of a preceding followed word of its meter, so it is, when used without it, neglected, indicating nothing at all. As for with it, although it indicates a meaning, its indication is not conventional, but rather its indication is like the indication of inverted words. And by this, the secret of the lack of synonymy between them appears to you. As for what the author mentioned, there is obscurity in it, for indication when isolated is not a condition in synonymy; do you not see that the attached pronoun and the detached pronoun are synonyms, and the attached pronoun if isolated indicates nothing at all? And synonymy may even occur in the original letters, although they have no indication when isolated. So reflect.

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition lesson explaining that there is no synonymy between the emphasized word (mu'akkad) and the emphasis word (mu'akkad) itself. In verbal emphasis (like repeating a word), the words are identical, so synonymy requires different words. In moral emphasis (like using 'nafs' or 'ayn'), the meaning differs. Synonymy requires different words and same meaning. Key Terms
تابع (tābi'): Follower: a word that follows another for reinforcement, e.g., 'basan' in 'hasan basan'. It has no independent meaning.
متبوع (matbū'): Followed: the word that is reinforced by the follower, e.g., 'hasan' in 'hasan basan'.
الضمير المتصل (al-ḍamīr al-muttaṣil): Attached pronoun: a pronoun attached to a word, e.g., 'hu' in 'ḍarabahu'. It has no meaning when isolated.

Key Takeaway
The follower in a rhyming pair is not a synonym because its indication is non-conventional, contrasting with attached pronouns which have conventional indication despite being meaningless alone.

The Inclusive Indication and Intention of Three Divorces in 'Tallaqi Nafsaki'
Analyzing the validity of intending three divorces in 'tallaqi nafsaki' via inclusive indication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of inclusive indication (dalalat al-tadammun) to derive that the phrase 'tallaqi nafsaki' permits the husband to intend three divorces, and rebut the objection that a single word cannot indicate multiple meanings.

Core Idea
The verb 'tallaqi' linguistically includes the infinitive 'talaq', which can be qualified by number, so intention of three is valid.

In Hanafi usul, the linguistic structure of a command can carry implicit meanings that affect legal rulings. This passage examines the phrase 'tallaqi nafsaki' (divorce yourself) and shows how the inclusive indication (dalalat al-tadammun) reveals the infinitive 'talaq', which can be specified for number. The author defends this against the objection that a single word cannot indicate many meanings by highlighting the speaker's intent and the duality of matter and form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its linguistic components
The phrase 'tallaqi nafsaki' is a command. Break it into verb 'tallaqi' and object 'nafsaki'. The verb is derived from the root t-l-q.
We focus on the verb, which is the locus of the ruling.
2
Apply dalalat al-tadammun to extract the infinitive
According to Arabic linguistics, the verb 'tallaqi' contains its infinitive 'talaq' by inclusive indication. Thus the command means 'bring about a divorce' (awjidi talaqan).
This is not idmar (insertion) but inherent inclusion.
3
Show that the infinitive allows specification for number
The infinitive 'talaq' can be qualified by adjectives of number (one, two, three). Therefore, the husband's intention of three is valid because the language permits it.
This is analogous to saying 'you are the divorce' or 'you are divorced with a divorce'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع آخر في قول الرجل لامرأته : (طلقي نفسك، يصح فيه نية الثلاث فوهم أنه من باب إضمار الكل) فإن الطلاق مضمر ليس ملفوظاً فأجيب بأنه متضمن للمصدر (لغة فلا إضمار (لأن معناه أوجدي طلاقاً) فيكون المصدر مدلولاً لغة بالتضمن (والمصدر يصح فيه نية الثلاث، كما في : أنت الطلاق، أو طالق طلاقاً فإنه يصح فيه نية الثلاث، ولقائل أن يقول : إنه قد سبق أن اللفظ المفرد لا يدل على معان كثيرة بوضع واحد وإن الدلالة التضمنية متحدة المطابقة فلا التصرف فيها، بل مثل هذه الدلالة مثل الالتزامية المنطقية، ولك أن تجيب عنه بأنه لا شك أن هذه الدلالة ملحوظة للمتكلم فإن ها هنا دلالتين المادة والهيئة والمادة تدل مطابقة على المصدر، وحينئذ فصح التصرف فيه بخلاف المدلول الالتزامي المنطقي الغير الملحوظ للمتكلم أن الحكم باتحاد الدلالتين أمر عسير جداً فتذكر (أقول) هذا (منقوض بنحو لا آكل فإنه أيضاً متضمن للمصدر، فيصح فيه نية أكل دون أكل ومأكول دون مأكول (فتأمل) إشارة إلى الجواب بأن المصدر المتضمن فيه نفس الأكل المصدر للفعل، وهو مطلق من حيث لا يجوز تقييده بحال، بخلاف طلقي، فإن المتضمن فيه مصدر آخر وهو الطلاق صالح لأن هو يتصرف فيه فيراد به طلاق دون طلاق هذا محصول ما في «الحاشية». ولك أن تفرق بأن أفراد الأكل باعتبار تقييده بمأكول دون مأكول كأكل التفاحة أو أكل الخبز لا يصح أن التقييد بالمفعول لم يعتبر ولم يلاحظ ، وأما أفراده باعتبار ذاته، وهي أنواع حركة اللحيين، فلا يلتفت إليه فيه عرفاً، بخلاف الطلاق من البائن والرجعي فتدبر (ونقض في المشهور بطالق) فإنه إذا قيل : أنت طالق لا يصح نية الثلاث، مع أن المصدر متضمن فيه أيضاً ودفع بأن الطلاق) المذكور فيه (وصفها وهو أثر التطليق، وتكرر الأثر بتكرر المؤثر) الذي هو التطليق (والمؤثر غير مكرر) فلا يتكرر الطلاق الذي من صفات المرأة، وإنما لا يتكرر التطليق المؤثر (لأن الثابت لتصحيح الخبرية من باب المقتضى فلا يقبل العموم وتفصيله أن : أنت طالق، وطلقتك، إخبار عن اتصاف المرأة بالطلاق فلا بد من وقوعه قبيل هذا الخبر ليصدق، فيثبت إيقاع من الزوج لتصحيح الخبرية، فهو من باب المقتضى الغير المقدر ولا عموم له ولا تعدد
Another subsidiary issue concerning a man's statement to his wife: 'Divorce yourself' (tallaqi nafsaki): it is valid to intend three divorces in it. Someone imagined that it is from the category of inserting the whole (idmar al-kull), because the divorce (talaq) is implicit, not uttered. So it was answered that it (the verb) contains the infinitive linguistically, so there is no insertion, because its meaning is 'bring about a divorce' (awjidi talaqan). Thus the infinitive is linguistically indicated by inclusion (al-dalala bi al-tadammun). And the infinitive allows the intention of three, as in 'you are the divorce' (anti al-talaq) or 'you are divorced with a divorce' (taliq talaqan), for it is valid to intend three. Someone may say that it has preceded that a single word does not indicate many meanings by one linguistic designation, and that the inclusive indication (al-dalala al-tadammuniyya) is one in terms of compliance (mutabaqa), so there is no room for manipulation in it; rather such indication is like the logical implication (al-iltizam al-mantiqi). You may answer that there is no doubt that this indication is intended by the speaker, for here there are two indications: that of the matter (al-madda) and that of the form (al-hay'a). The matter indicates compliance the infinitive, and then manipulation is valid in it, unlike the logical implication which is not intended by the speaker. The ruling of unity of the two indications is very difficult, so remember. I say: this is criticized by the example of 'I do not eat' (la akul), for it also contains the infinitive, so it would be valid to intend eating without eating and eaten without eaten. 'Reflect' refers to the answer that the infinitive contained in it is the actual eating which is the infinitive of the verb, and it is absolute with respect to not being restricted in any state, unlike 'tallaqi', for the infinitive contained in it is another infinitive, which is divorce (talaq), and it is suitable for manipulation, so that one may intend a divorce without divorce. This is the gist of what is in the Hashiya. And you may distinguish that the individual instances of eating in terms of its restriction by what is eaten, like eating an apple or eating bread, are not valid because restriction by the object was not considered; but its individual instances in terms of its essence, which are types of jaw movement, are not considered customarily. Unlike divorce between bain and raj'i, so reflect. And it is criticized in the well-known case by 'divorced' (taliq): for when one says 'you are divorced' (anti taliq), it is not valid to intend three, although the infinitive is also contained in it. It is repelled by the fact that the divorce mentioned in it is a description of her (the wife), and it is the effect of the act of divorcing (tatliq). The effect may be repeated by the repetition of the cause, but the cause is not repeated, so the divorce which is from the attributes of the woman is not repeated. Rather, the effective divorcing is not repeated because what is established for correcting the predicative statement is from the category of al-muqtada, so it does not admit generality. The detail: 'you are divorced' and 'I divorced you' are reports of the woman being described with divorce, so it must have occurred prior to this report for it to be truthful. Thus an occurrence from the husband is established for correcting the predicative statement; it is from the category of al-muqtada which is not specified, and it has no generality and no multiplicity.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a legal analysis of the phrase 'tallaqi nafsaki' (divorce yourself) and whether the husband can intend three divorces. The author clarifies that the verb 'tallaqi' linguistically includes the infinitive (talaq) through the indication of inclusion (dalalat al-tadammun). Therefore, it is not a case of 'idmar al-kull' (inserting the whole) because the infinitive is already contained. Consequently, the husband can intend three divorces, just as in expressions like 'anti al-talaq' or 'taliq talaqan'. The author then addresses objections: a word cannot indicate many meanings by one designation, but the response is that the matter (madda) indicates the infinitive directly, and manipulation (tasarrub) is possible because it is intended by the speaker, unlike logical implication. Then an objection is raised using 'la akul' (I do not eat): it also contains the infinitive, but one cannot intend different types of eating. The answer is that the infinitive 'akl' is absolute and cannot be restricted, whereas 'talaq' is divisible into types (bain and raj'i). Finally, the case of 'anti taliq' (you are divorced) is distinguished: it is a description of the wife, implying a single occurrence of divorce necessary for truthful predication, so it does not admit three. The lesson demonstrates how usul principles like dalalat al-tadammun and the nature of the infinitive affect fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الدلالة التضمنية (al-dalāla al-taḍammuniyya): Inclusive indication: a word's meaning includes a constituent part, e.g., 'tallaqi' includes the infinitive 'talaq'.
المصدر (al-maṣdar): Verbal noun; in this context, the infinitive of the verb which can be modified (e.g., by number).
المقتضى (al-muqtaḍā): What is required (by the context) for the truth of a statement; here, the occurrence of divorce is presupposed for the report 'anti taliq' to be true.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason that intending three divorces is valid in 'tallaqi nafsaki'?
A) Because the husband explicitly says 'three'
B) Because the verb 'tallaqi' includes the infinitive 'talaq' which can be qualified by number
C) Because the phrase is ambiguous and any number is possible
D) Because the wife can choose the number

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the inclusive indication (dalalat al-tadammun) in a verb reveals the infinitive, which can be qualified by number, permitting intention of multiple units unless context prevents it.

Mantuq and Mafhum
advanced
9 min
Distinguishing 'Tallaqi Nafsaki' from 'Anti Taliq' and 'La Akul'
Distinguishing the ruling for 'tallaqi nafsaki' from counterexamples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish why the inclusive indication allows intention of three in 'tallaqi nafsaki' but not in 'anti taliq' or 'la akul', by analyzing the nature of the infinitive and the role of muqtada.

Core Idea
In 'anti taliq', the description of the wife requires only one divorce for truthfulness; in 'la akul', the infinitive is absolute and not divisible.

After establishing the validity of intending three divorces in 'tallaqi nafsaki', the passage addresses two counterexamples: the negation 'la akul' and the descriptive phrase 'anti taliq'. These reveal important qualifications on the principle of inclusive indication. The infinitive in 'la akul' is absolute and cannot be restricted, while 'anti taliq' is a descriptive report that implies a single occurrence due to the nature of muqtada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two problematic cases
The passage raises two critiques: (1) 'la akul' (I do not eat) contains the infinitive of eating, yet one cannot intend a specific type of eating; (2) 'anti taliq' (you are divorced) is a description of the woman, not a command, and does not allow three.
These are presented as 'naqd' (objections) to the general rule.
2
Analyze the case of 'la akul'
The infinitive 'akl' (eating) is absolute by nature; it cannot be restricted to specific objects (like apple or bread) because the object is not part of the infinitive. Additionally, its essence (types of jaw movement) is not customarily considered. Thus manipulation is invalid.
Contrast with 'talaq', which is divisible into types (bain and raj'i) and is customarily specified.
3
Analyze the case of 'anti taliq'
'Anti taliq' is a predicate describing the woman with the attribute 'taliq' (divorced). For the report to be true, the divorce must have occurred. This establishes an occurrence of divorce by way of muqtada (what is presupposed for truthfulness). Muqtada has no generality or multiplicity; it only establishes the minimum necessary.
Thus only one divorce is implied.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Mantuq and Mafhum
intermediate
8 min
Defining Al-Iqtida: Contextual Implication in Hanafi Usul
Definition of al-iqtida as a type of mantuq indication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-iqtida, distinguish it from other types of dalalat al-mantuq, and apply it to identify implicit conditions in legal texts.

Core Idea
Al-iqtida: the explicit text implies what is necessary for its own validity, without which it would be false.

Al-iqtida (contextual implication) is a key concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh that allows the mujtahid to infer an unstated condition essential for the explicit statement to be valid. It belongs to dalalat al-mantuq because it arises from the explicit words themselves, not from silence. This lesson unpacks its precise definition and how it applies to legal texts.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the term and its category
Recognise that al-iqtida is a type of dalalat al-mantuq (explicit indication) – it is not a mafhum. The explicit speech (muqtadi) is the source of the implication.
Many students confuse iqtida with mafhum; iqtida is still mantuq-based.
2
2. Break down the definition into components
The definition states: 'indication of the explicit speech for something on which its validity depends'. Identify the three key elements: the explicit speech (mantuq), the implied thing (muqtada), and the dependency (validity).
Validity here means the speech being truthful (sidq) for reports.
3
3. Recognise the scope for reports
The text specifies that for reports (akhbar), the implied element is truthfulness – either rationally (e.g., speaker is sane) or legally (e.g., speaker is adult). This restricts iqtida to statements that must be true.
For non-reports, iqtida may apply differently, but the definition focuses on reports.
4
4. Distinguish between muqtadi and muqtada
The muqtadi is the explicit speech; the muqtada is the implied condition. The muqtadi does not include the muqtada in its wording; rather it requires it for validity. The muqtada is considered as a premise to correct the muqtadi.
Example: 'You are free' implies ownership – the explicit speech is the utterance, the implied condition is ownership.
5
5. Apply to a legal example
Take the Quranic verse 'And let a scribe write between you with justice' (2:282). The explicit command implies that the scribe is just (adl) because the validity of the contract depends on a just scribe. This is iqtida.
The implied condition is not stated but is necessary for the command to be fulfilled validly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها الاقتضاء، وهو دلالة المنطوق على ما يتوقف صحته عليه) وهي في الأخبار تكون بالصدق ( عقلاً أو شرعاً) واحترز بقوله دلالة المنطوق عن المقدر، فإن اللفظ المقدر هناك دال لا المنطوق المقتضي (فيعتبر هذا المعنى المدلول (مقدماً تصحيحاً للمقتضي)
And among them is al-iqtida, which is the indication of the explicit speech (mantuq) for something on which its validity depends. This, in reports (akhbar), is truthfulness, rationally or legally. He restricted by his saying 'indication of the explicit speech' to exclude the implied (muqaddar), for the implied word there is what indicates, not the explicit speech that necessitates. So this meaning (the implied) is considered as a premise to correct the necessitating [explicit speech].
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage defines al-iqtida (contextual implication) as a type of dalalat al-mantuq (explicit indication). Specifically, it is the implication of the spoken words for something that is necessary for the validity of that speech. For example, in the statement 'You are free' (anta hurr), the implicit condition is that the speaker owns the slave; without that condition, the statement would be false. The text specifies that for reports (akhbar), the implied element is truthfulness, either rationally (such as the speaker being sane) or legally (such as the speaker being of legal age). The author distinguishes between the explicit speech (mantuq) and the implicit (muqaddar): the explicit speech is what necessitates (muqtadi), while the implicit meaning is what is necessitated (muqtada). The implicit meaning is not explicitly uttered but is considered as if it were a premise to correct (make valid) the explicit speech. This is a common usul definition of iqtida.

Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida): The implication of explicit speech for something without which the speech's validity (truthfulness) would be null, either rationally or legally.
دلالة المنطوق (dalalat al-mantuq): The indication derived from the uttered words themselves, as opposed to mafhum.
صدق (sidq): Truthfulness; the required quality of a report for iqtida to apply.
مقتضي (muqtadi): The explicit speech that necessitates (requires) an implied element for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does al-iqtida specifically refer to?
A) The indication of the unspoken meaning opposed to the explicit.
B) The implication of the explicit speech for something necessary for its validity.
C) A type of qiyas that uses hidden analogy.
D) The inclusion of a part in the whole as in fahwa.

Key Takeaway
Al-iqtida is a powerful tool in Hanafi usul that allows the mujtahid to infer conditions essential for the validity of explicit statements, especially in reports where truthfulness is required.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Mafhum al-Mukhalafa: Definition, Condition, and Hanafi Rejection
Defines mafhum al-mukhalafa and presents Hanafi arguments rejecting its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mafhum al-mukhalafa, state the condition required by those who accept it, and explain the three Hanafi proofs for rejecting it as a valid linguistic proof.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is always invalid because the condition of 'no other benefit' is never satisfied in any speech.

Mafhum al-mukhalafa is a key concept in usul al-fiqh that some schools use to derive rulings from the opposite of what is stated. The Hanafi school, however, rejects this concept entirely, arguing that its foundational condition can never be verified, especially in the speech of the Lawgiver. This lesson unpacks the definition, the condition, and the three robust Hanafi arguments that demonstrate why mafhum al-mukhalafa cannot be relied upon in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Define mafhum al-mukhalafa and its condition
Start by understanding the term: it is the inferred opposite ruling for what is not mentioned based on a description in the spoken ruling. The condition for its validity is the absence of any other benefit (fā'ida) for mentioning the description besides negating the ruling from others.
This condition is agreed upon by those who accept mafhum al-mukhalafa.
2
Identify the schools of acceptance and rejection
Note that Shafi'is, Hanbalis, Ash'aris, and some Mu'tazila accept it, while Hanafis, al-Baqillani, al-Ghazali, and most Mu'tazila reject it. The Hanafi position is designated as 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen view).
Al-Ghazali is a Shafi'i but rejects this concept.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi proof: the condition is unknowable
The first argument: the condition of 'no other benefit' can never be known with certainty, because the number of possible benefits is unlimited, especially in divine speech. Even if one assumes no benefit, that assumption itself becomes a benefit, so the condition is never met.
This is a negative proof showing the impossibility of verification.
4
Analyze the second Hanafi proof: a constant benefit always exists
The second argument: there is always a benefit in mentioning a description: it identifies the subject or makes it a title. Thus, a diverting factor (sārif) is always present, preventing the concept from being established.
The benefit of 'al-ta'bīr 'an al-mahkūm 'alayh' is unavoidable.
5
Analyze the third Hanafi proof: distinction between khabar and insha'
The third argument: if mafhum were valid, it would apply equally to reports (khabar) and performatives (insha'), but in reports the absence of mention does not imply absence in reality, while in performatives the ruling is tied to utterance. This distinction blocks the application of mafhum to legal rulings.
This is the most technical argument, involving the nature of obligation.

للمفهوم الثاني فافهم) ولك أن تجيب عن أصل الإيراد بأنه لا يمكن الظن بفقدان الفائدة فإن الفوائد غير محصورة في عدد ولو ظناً حتى يعلم الانتفاء أو يظن ثم هي لكثرتها لا يتحقق مادة ينتفي فيها الجميع بأسرها إلا نادراً، إذ لا أقل من أن الفائدة التعبير عن المحكوم عليه بالموصوف بالصفة وجعله عنواناً له كما في التعبير باللقب، وعلى هذا يندفع ما يورد أن مقصودهم أن الكلام موضوع لنفي الحكم عن المسكوت والفوائد الأخرى صارفة عنه ، فإذا لم يظهر فائدة أخرى يظن به في سائر الحقائق فلا يضر عدم معرفة انحصار الفوائد، وذلك لأن فائدة التعبير عن المحكوم عليه أو متعلقاته لا يخلو عنها تركيب، فوجود الصارف لازم فلا دلالة على انتفاء الحكم أصلاً فتدبر (و) لنا (ثانياً ترك المسكوت محلاً للاستدلال بالأصل أو تركه محلاً للاجتهاد والنظر بالقياس إلى المنطوق أو إلى غيره فائدة (لازمة لا يخلو الموصوف بالصفة عنها، وثبوت المفهوم متوقف على عدم الفوائد بأسرها فلا يثبت المفهوم أصلاً، قيل: مقصودهم ثابت؛ ومدلول للكلام ما لم يظهر صارف من الفوائد فاحتمال الفوائد الأخرى احتمال ،الصوارف واحتمالها لا يضر في الظن بالحقيقة وهذا غير واف فإنه لو سلم أن ذلك أن عباراتهم تنبو عنه، فالفوائد الأخرى إذا تحققت لم يتحقق المفهوم فإن الحقيقة لا تتحقق عند وجود الصوارف عنها، والفوائد المذكورة لا يخلو كلام ما عن واحد منها، فلا يخلو كلام ما عن الصارف عن الحقيقة، فلا تتحقق أصلاً فافهم ولا تزل فإنه مزلة (و) لنا (ثالثاً : لو ثبت) المفهوم الثبت في الخبر لأن العلة الحذر عن عدم الفائدة) وهو مشترك بينهما (والتالي باطل لأنه لو قال في الشام الغنم السائمة لم يدل على عدم المعلوفة فيها (ضرورة والتزامه مكابرة، كذا في شرح المختصر » قال في الحاشية» مع كونه مكابرة قد التزمه بعضهم حتى قال التفتازاني : والحق عدم الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، هذا والحق أنه لا مكابرة فيه، فإن مدلول هذا الكلام ليس في الشام المعلوفة، إلا أنه يمنع عنه مانع خارجي كالعلم بوجود المعلوفة فيه، وهذا صارف لا يضر في دلالة نفس الكلام ثم ادعاء الإجماع على عدم المفهوم في الخبر لو صح تم الكلام (وأجيب بأن في الخبر لا يلزم من عدم الإخبار العدم) للحكم (خارجاً) وغاية ما فيه عدم الإخبار عن حال المسكوت فلا يلزم عدم الحكم فيه في الخارج، إذ لا دخل للإخبار في ثبوت الحكم أو انتفائه في الخارج بخلاف الحكم الشرعي) الثابت الإنشاء فإنه لا خارج له فوجوب الزكاة هو قوله : أوجبت فإذا انتفى القول) الذي هو الإنشاء انتفى الوجوب لأنه هو المثبت وقد انتفى في المسكوت :القول فانتفى الحكم فاتضح الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، فالملازمة ممنوعة (قال ابن الحاجب هذا دقيق، ورد بأنه قول بنفي المفهوم وكونه مسكوت عنه لا كونه محكوماً بنقيض الحكم لأن حاصله عدم التعرض للحكم (لغة) وإنما يلزم الانتفاء لانتفاء المثبت وبه نقول أيضاً، فإنه قول ببقاء المسكوت على الأصل فافهم فإنه ظاهر جداً واستدل أولاً بأنه لو ثبت المفهوم فإما بالعقل أو النقل والعقل لا مدخل له في إثبات الأوضاع والنقل إما بالتواتر حقيقة أو حكماً أو بالآحاد (ولا تواتر) ههنا (حقيقة أو حكماً كالإجماع أو كاستقراء رفع الفاعل اتفاقاً بيننا وبينكم وأيضاً لو كان كذلك لم ينكره الأئمة ذوو اليد الطولى في الاستقراء والتتبع والآحاد لا تفيد في مثله لاشتراك الكل في سبب العلم، والتزم بعضهم التواتر وهو مكابرة، وإلا فكان الوضع مقطوعاً، بل تكون الدلالة عليه مقطوعة عند عدم الصارف كما هو شأن سائر الحقائق، وهذا خلاف الإجماع (وأجيب) لا نسلم أن الآحاد لا تفيد بل) تفيد للقطع بقبول الآحاد عن الأصمعي والخليل مثلا) في وضع الألفاظ (أقول : الاستقراء الصحيح دل) على أن وجود أصل الدلالة قطعي في الهيئات النوعية للتراكيب المتعارفة عند الآحاد من العوام والخواص، وهذا لأن كل أحد يتكلم بهذه التركيبات
Third article on linguistic principles. It is called 'lahn al-khitab', and sometimes 'mafhum mukhalafa', which is the establishment of the opposite of the ruling of the spoken expression, whether negation or affirmation, for the unmentioned. It is called 'dalil al-khitab', and its condition (i.e., the condition of its verification) is the absence of what necessitates specification by mention, other than negating the ruling from the unmentioned, and what necessitates other than that (such as the appearance of priority or equality) because in these two cases, the unmentioned is equal to the mentioned in ruling by indication or analogy, and the speech is in the manner of custom, for then the apparent is speech according to custom, not negation of the ruling, and it being an answer to the questioner about the state of the mentioned, for then the purpose is matching the question, and the speaker's ignorance of the state of what is not mentioned, so it does not indicate negation at all due to specification by mention, and other such benefits. It (i.e., mafhum al-mukhalafa) has divisions: among them is 'mafhum al-sifa', which is the establishment of the opposite of the ruling of the spoken expression for that which does not have the attribute among the individuals of the described. Al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, al-Ash'ari, and a group held it, and the Hanafis, Abu Bakr (al-Baqillani), Imam al-Ghazali (both from the Shafi'is), and the Mu'tazila negated it, and it is the chosen position. The locus of dispute is linguistic indication, meaning that the construction is linguistically placed for the concept when there is no other benefit according to them, contrary to us. It is said that it is placed or commonly used (not like the subtleties of eloquent speakers) for there is no dispute that eloquent speakers sometimes intend it, not that they always intend it when there is another benefit, such that speech devoid of negation of the ruling from what is other than it and without another benefit would not be eloquent, leading to the objection that the speech of the Lawgiver is at the highest degree of eloquence, so the concept would necessarily follow, and it is the basis of rulings, and we have little need for non-eloquent speech. [Proof] Firstly: I say the indication of the concept is theoretical and always unknown, and no linguistic indication is like that necessarily. So no concept is by linguistic indication. The first premise is that it is dependent on the absence of another benefit by agreement, and that is always unknown, for the number of benefits is unknown so that their absence can be known, especially in the speech of the Lawgiver, for intellects are incapable of encompassing His benefits. If it is said: perhaps one assumes the absence of benefit and thus assumes the concept, and we do not need certainty, for we do not claim certainty of the concept. I say: this assumption (i.e., assumption of no other benefit) is actually an assumption of the concept from among the benefits, so its absence must be known, but it remains unknown. Rather, the concept is negated entirely. You may also say: assumption may be considered by intent (as when the situation requires the speaker to mention speech that gives the impression of specification and restriction while he does not intend it, so there is no indication of negation of the ruling from what is other than it, but rather the purpose is only illusion, as in the marginalia) or assumption may be considered incidentally (by speaking to convey a ruling without intending another benefit, so one assumes the absence of benefit and the negated benefit is the first, and the condition for the second concept, so understand). You may also answer the original objection by saying that it is impossible to assume the lack of benefit, for benefits are not limited in number even by assumption, so that their absence can be known or assumed; moreover, due to their abundance, a case where all are absent is rarely realized, for at the very least there is the benefit of expressing the subject of the ruling with the attribute and making it a title for it, as in the expression by a title. On this basis, what is objected is refuted: that their intention is that speech is placed for negating the ruling from the unmentioned and other benefits divert from it, so if no other benefit appears, one assumes it in the remaining cases, and not knowing the limitation of benefits does not harm. That is because the benefit of expressing the subject of the ruling or its attachments is never absent from any construction, so the diverting factor is always present, so there is no indication of negation of the ruling at all, so ponder. Secondly, leaving the unmentioned as a place for inference by the original principle or leaving it as a place for ijtihad and consideration by analogy to the mentioned or to other things is a necessary benefit that the described with the attribute never lacks, and the establishment of the concept depends on the absence of all benefits, so the concept is not established at all. It is said: their intention is established; the meaning of the speech is as long as no diverting benefit appears, so the probability of other benefits is probability of diverting factors, and probability does not harm the assumption of the truth. This is insufficient, for even if one concedes that their expressions are incompatible with it, when other benefits are realized, the concept is not realized, for the truth is not realized when diverting factors are present, and the mentioned benefits are never absent from any speech, so no speech is free from the diverting factor from the truth, so it is never realized. So understand and do not slip, for it is a slippery place. Thirdly, if the concept were established, it would be established in reports because the cause is caution regarding the absence of benefit, and that is common between them, but the consequent is false, because if one says 'in Syria, grazing sheep,' it does not indicate the absence of fed sheep there necessarily, and insisting on it is obstinacy, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. The marginalia says, despite being obstinacy, some have insisted on it, even al-Taftazani said: the truth is that there is no difference between report and construction. This, and the truth is there is no obstinacy in it, for the meaning of this statement is that there are no fed sheep in Syria, but an external preventer prevents it, like knowledge of the existence of fed sheep there, and this is a diverting factor that does not harm the indication of the speech itself. Then claiming consensus on the absence of the concept in reports, if valid, would settle the matter. It is answered that in reports, the lack of information does not entail the lack of the ruling externally, and at most it is the lack of information about the state of the unmentioned, so the lack of the ruling externally is not entailed, for information has no role in the establishment or negation of the ruling externally, unlike the legal ruling established by construction, for it has no external existence. Thus the obligation of zakat is His statement 'I obligated', so if the statement (which is the construction) is absent, the obligation is absent, for it is the establisher, and the statement is absent for the unmentioned, so the ruling is absent. Thus the distinction between report and construction becomes clear, so the entailment is denied. Ibn al-Hajib said this is precise. It is rejected as being a statement of negating the concept and that being unmentioned does not entail being ruled by the opposite, because the gist is not addressing the ruling linguistically, and the negation follows only from the negation of the establisher, and that is what we also say, for it is a statement that the unmentioned remains on the original principle, so understand, for it is very apparent. He argued firstly that if the concept were established, it would be either by reason or by transmission, and reason has no role in establishing linguistic conventions, and transmission is either by tawatur actually or effectively, or by ahad, and there is no tawatur here actually or effectively (like consensus or like the induction of raising the agent by agreement between us and you). Also, if it were so, the imams of deep knowledge in induction and investigation would not have denied it, and ahad reports are not beneficial in such matters due to the commonality of everyone in the cause of knowledge. Some insisted on tawatur, which is obstinacy, otherwise the convention would be certain, and the indication would be certain when there is no diverting factor, as is the case with all truths, and this is contrary to consensus. It is answered: we do not concede that ahad reports are not beneficial; rather, they are beneficial for certainty by accepting ahad reports from al-Asma'i and al-Khalil, for example, in the placement of words. I say: correct induction shows that the existence of the original indication is certain in the specific forms of customary constructions among the common and elite, because everyone speaks with these constructions.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from Ibn 'Abd al-Shakur's commentary on Musallam al-Thubut defines the concept of 'mafhum al-mukhalafa' (implied meaning of opposition) and presents the Hanafi school's rejection of its validity as a linguistic proof. The author first clarifies terminology: this concept is also called 'lahn al-khitab' or 'dalil al-khitab'. It means that when a ruling is stated for a specific description, the opposite ruling is implied for what lacks that description. The condition for its validity, according to those who accept it (Shafi'is, Hanbalis, Ash'aris), is that there is no other benefit in mentioning the description besides negating the ruling from others. Such benefits include: the description showing priority or equality (in which case the unmentioned shares the same ruling by stronger implication or analogy), customary speech patterns, answering a specific question, or the speaker's ignorance of the state of the unmentioned. The Hanafis (along with al-Baqillani, al-Ghazali, and the Mu'tazila) reject this entirely. The author gives three proofs. First: the condition of 'no other benefit' is unknowable, especially in divine speech whose wisdoms are infinite; one can never be certain that no other benefit exists. Even if one assumes no benefit, that assumption is itself a benefit (the assumption of the concept), so the condition is never met. Second: there is always a benefit in specifying a description: it serves to identify the subject or make it a title, which is a constant benefit. Since the concept requires the absence of all benefits, and such absence never occurs, the concept never holds. Third: if the concept were valid, it would apply to both informative (khabari) and performative (insha'i) statements equally, but in informative statements (like 'in Syria, grazing sheep'), the negation of fed sheep is not necessarily implied because external knowledge may override. Moreover, in performative statements (like 'I obligated zakat'), the ruling is tied to the utterance itself, so if the utterance is absent for the unmentioned, the ruling is truly absent. Thus there is a distinction between report and construction, which the opponents fail to see. The Hanafi position is that the unmentioned remains on its original ruling (istishab al-hal), not that it has the opposite ruling. The passage concludes with a discussion of the method of proving linguistic conventions, arguing that the supposed consensus and tawatur for mafhum is not established, and that the inductive evidence actually shows that the concept is not part of the language.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implied meaning that establishes the opposite ruling for what is not mentioned, based on the specific wording of the mentioned ruling.
مفهوم الصفة (mafhum al-sifa): The implied meaning that establishes the opposite ruling for individuals lacking the attribute mentioned in the description.
دليل الخطاب (dalil al-khitab): Another term for mafhum al-mukhalafa, referring to the proof derived from the wording of the address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for mafhum al-mukhalafa to be valid according to those who accept it?
A) The description must be a cause ('illa) for the ruling.
B) There must be no other benefit in mentioning the description besides negating the ruling from others.
C) The speaker must be unaware of the state of the unmentioned.
D) The speech must be in the form of a question and answer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects mafhum al-mukhalafa because its condition (no other benefit) is never verified in actual speech, making it an unreliable basis for deriving legal rulings.

Mantuq and Mafhum
intermediate
8 min
The Necessity of Sarif: Why Mafhum al-Mukhalafa Cannot Be Established
Debate on whether Mafhum al-Mukhalafa is a valid legal indicator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument that every speech contains a benefit (fa'ida) which acts as a sarif, and apply this to the example of grazing sheep to explain why mafhum al-mukhalafa is not established.

Core Idea
The condition for mafhum al-mukhalafa is never met: every speech has a benefit that diverts from the literal meaning.

In this passage, the author presents the first of several Hanafi arguments against Mafhum al-Mukhalafa (the concept of opposition). The core idea is that for a concept to indicate the opposite ruling, the description in the text must have no other benefit—yet every description in legal speech serves some purpose. This 'benefit' acts as a diverting factor (sarif) that blocks the concept from being taken as a legal indicator. We'll walk through this argument and its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for mafhum al-mukhalafa
The concept requires that the description have no other benefit in the speech; otherwise, the literal meaning is diverted. The text states 'ما لم يظهر صارف من الفوائد' (unless a diverting factor appears from the benefits).
2
Show that every speech necessarily contains such benefits
The author argues that every legal text has a benefit—e.g., specifying a ruling, defining a category, or preventing misunderstanding. Therefore, the condition is never satisfied.
The phrase 'لا يخلو كلام ما عن الصارف عن الحقيقة' (no speech is free from a diverting factor from the truth) is key.
3
Conclude that mafhum al-mukhalafa cannot be established
Since the diverting factor is always present, the concept of opposition never comes into effect. The unmentioned case (maskut) remains on its original legal principle (al-asl).
This is the Hanafi position: the concept is not a valid indicator.
4
Apply to the example of grazing sheep
In the example 'grazing sheep require zakat', the description 'grazing' has a benefit—it specifies a condition for zakat. That benefit diverts from implying that non-grazing sheep are exempt. So no opposite ruling is derived.
The text says: 'لو قال في الشام الغنم السائمة لم يدل على عدم المعلوفة فيها' (if he said 'in Syria, grazing sheep', it does not indicate the absence of non-grazing).
