مقصودهم مع فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الأول المحكوم عليه أو متعلقاته لا يخلو عنها تركيب، فوجود الصارف لازم فلا دلالة على انتفاء الحكم أصلاً فتدبر (و) لنا (ثانياً ترك المسكوت محلاً للاستدلال بالأصل أو تركه محلاً للاجتهاد والنظر بالقياس إلى المنطوق أو إلى غيره فائدة (لازمة لا يخلو الموصوف بالصفة عنها، وثبوت المفهوم متوقف على عدم الفوائد بأسرها فلا يثبت المفهوم أصلاً، قيل: مقصودهم ثابت؛ ومدلول للكلام ما لم يظهر صارف من الفوائد فاحتمال الفوائد الأخرى احتمال ،الصوارف واحتمالها لا يضر في الظن بالحقيقة وهذا غير واف فإنه لو سلم أن ذلك أن عباراتهم تنبو عنه، فالفوائد الأخرى إذا تحققت لم يتحقق المفهوم فإن الحقيقة لا تتحقق عند وجود الصوارف عنها، والفوائد المذكورة لا يخلو كلام ما عن واحد منها، فلا يخلو كلام ما عن الصارف عن الحقيقة، فلا تتحقق أصلاً فافهم ولا تزل فإنه مزلة (و) لنا (ثالثاً : لو ثبت) المفهوم الثبت في الخبر لأن العلة الحذر عن عدم الفائدة) وهو مشترك بينهما (والتالي باطل لأنه لو قال في الشام الغنم السائمة لم يدل على عدم المعلوفة فيها (ضرورة والتزامه مكابرة، كذا في شرح المختصر » قال في الحاشية» مع كونه مكابرة قد التزمه بعضهم حتى قال التفتازاني : والحق عدم الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، هذا والحق أنه لا مكابرة فيه، فإن مدلول هذا الكلام ليس في الشام المعلوفة، إلا أنه يمنع عنه مانع خارجي كالعلم بوجود المعلوفة فيه، وهذا صارف لا يضر في دلالة نفس الكلام ثم ادعاء الإجماع على عدم المفهوم في الخبر لو صح تم الكلام (وأجيب بأن في الخبر لا يلزم من عدم الإخبار العدم) للحكم (خارجاً) وغاية ما فيه عدم الإخبار عن حال المسكوت فلا يلزم عدم الحكم فيه في الخارج، إذ لا دخل للإخبار في ثبوت الحكم أو انتفائه في الخارج بخلاف الحكم الشرعي) الثابت الإنشاء فإنه لا خارج له فوجوب الزكاة هو قوله : أوجبت فإذا انتفى القول) الذي هو الإنشاء انتفى الوجوب لأنه هو المثبت وقد انتفى في المسكوت :القول فانتفى الحكم فاتضح الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، فالملازمة ممنوعة (قال ابن الحاجب هذا دقيق، ورد بأنه قول بنفي المفهوم وكونه مسكوت عنه لا كونه محكوماً بنقيض الحكم لأن حاصله عدم التعرض للحكم (لغة) وإنما يلزم الانتفاء لانتفاء المثبت وبه نقول أيضاً، فإنه قول ببقاء المسكوت على الأصل فافهم فإنه ظاهر جداً واستدل أولاً بأنه لو ثبت المفهوم فإما بالعقل أو النقل والعقل لا مدخل له في إثبات الأوضاع والنقل إما بالتواتر حقيقة أو حكماً أو بالآحاد (ولا تواتر) ههنا (حقيقة أو حكماً كالإجماع أو كاستقراء رفع الفاعل اتفاقاً بيننا وبينكم وأيضاً لو كان كذلك لم ينكره الأئمة ذوو اليد الطولى في الاستقراء والتتبع والآحاد لا تفيد في مثله لاشتراك الكل في سبب العلم، والتزم بعضهم التواتر وهو مكابرة، وإلا فكان الوضع مقطوعاً، بل تكون الدلالة عليه مقطوعة عند عدم الصارف كما هو شأن سائر الحقائق، وهذا خلاف الإجماع (وأجيب) لا نسلم أن الآحاد لا تفيد بل) تفيد للقطع بقبول الآحاد عن الأصمعي والخليل مثلا) في وضع الألفاظ (أقول : الاستقراء الصحيح دل) على أن وجود أصل الدلالة قطعي في الهيئات النوعية للتراكيب المتعارفة عند الآحاد من العوام والخواص، وهذا لأن كل أحد يتكلم بهذه التركيبات ويفيد بها ما في ضميره، وكذا يستفيد بها إذا خوطب فيعلم كل أحد معناه، فسبب العلم مشترك بين الكل بخلاف التراكيب القليلة الاستعمال، فإنه يجوز أن لا تكون قطعية ولا معلومة عند الكل، بل عند البعض فقط ففي مثله لا تقبل الآحاد البتة بل لا يبعد أن يقطع بخطأ الواحد الناقل (وإن قبل في (المواد الجزئية لجواز سماع واحد دون آخر وتركيب الموصوف والصفة متعارف عند الكل فلو كان دالاً على الحكم المخالف في المسكوت لكان قطعياً متواتراً ولا تقبل فيه الآحاد فافهم، فقد ثبت المطلوب بأقوم حجة لا يدحضها شبهة (قيل) في حواشي مرزاجان: الاستدلال بهذا الوجه على نفي المفهوم غير صحيح، ويقال : دليلكم على النفي إما عقلي وهو) أي العقل (لا يستقل أو نقلي إلى آخره أي فإما متواتر حقيقة أو حكماً وليس كذلك، أو أحادي، ولا يكفي في مثل هذا، وهذا الإيراد نقض إجمالي ويمكن أن يحرر معارضة بأن القول بنفي المفهوم باطل، فإن الدليل المقام عليه عقلي أو نقلي الخ... (أقول) دليلنا عقلي مع نقلي قاطع و إذا فرض أن لا علة (له أي للوضع إلا النقل تواتراً فبعدمه) أي التواتر (يعلم عدمه بالضرورة) وههنا معلوم قطعاً أن لا تواتر في النقل البتة، فيعلم أن لا دلالة أصلاً، إذ علتها ليست إلا التواتر فحسب وهذا ليس باستقلال للعقل حتى لا يقبل بل دوران مع النقل) وهو غير منكر (تدبر) فإنه لا يتجاوز عنه الحق (و) استدل (ثانياً لو صح) المفهوم (لما صح أذ زكاة السائمة والمعلوفة لا مجتمعاً أي في جملة (ولا متفرقاً) أي في جملتين لأن وزانه حينئذٍ وزان) قولك: لا تقل له أف (واضربه في كونه جمعاً بين متنافيين، فإن قوله أد زكاة السائمة يدل على عدم وجوب زكاة المعلوفة، وإذا عطف المعلوفة دل على وجوبها، كما أن لا تقل له أف يقتضي النهي عن الضرب واضربه أمر به (وأجيب بأنه) أي مفهوم المخالفة (ليس كمفهوم الموافقة لقطعية ذلك أي مفهوم الموافقة (وظنية هذا) أي مفهوم المخالفة ويضمحل الضعيف مع القوي الذي هو منطوق والمعلوفة فليس ههنا مفهوم لمنع القوي ولك أن تقرر الدليل بأنه لو كان المفهوم مدلولاً للكلام لفهم المتنافيان في المثال المذكور وإن كان يترك أحدهما للظنية كما يفهم المتنافيان فيما إذا تعارض المنطوقان أحدهما ظني ثم يترك الظني، وليس الأمر كذلك، بل لا يحضر المفهوم بالبال فليتأمل فيه (و) استدل (ثالثاً : لو ثبت المفهوم الثبت التعارض لثبوت المخالفة بين المفهوم والمنطوق أو المفهوم الآخر كثيراً كقوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبوا أَضْعَفًا مُضَعَفَةٌ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٠] ) فإن مفهومه أكل الربا إذا لم يكن أضعافاً، وهو مخالف للنصوص المحرمة للربا القليل أيضاً (وهو) أي التعارض (خلاف الأصل لا يصار إليه إلا بدليل ولا دليل فإن أقيم فبعد صحته كان دليلاً معارضاً لدليلكم (لظنيتهما) فيتساقطان فلا يثبت المفهوم، ولعله أراد بالتعارض التخالف المانع اجتماعهما مطلقاً، فإنه يكفي في المطلوب لا التعارض بمعنى تقاوم الحجتين المتساويتين في القوة حتى يرد أن وجود التعارض كثيراً غير بين فالتعادل في حيز الخفاء فافهم (وأجيب) بأنه (منقوض بحجية خبر الواحد فإنه لو كان حجة لوقع التعارض، لأن أكثر الآحاد متعارضة فلا يصار إليه إلا بالدليل، وإن أقيم يكون معارضاً لدليلنا فيتساقطان والأصل عدم
Their intention with Fawatih al-Rahamut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut Part One: The subject or its attributes cannot be separated from structure, so the existence of a diverting factor is necessary; thus there is no indication of the negation of the ruling at all, so reflect. (And) for us (secondly: leaving the unmentioned as a place for inference by the original principle, or leaving it as a place for ijtihad and consideration by analogy to the explicit or to other [texts] is a necessary benefit that the described [thing] cannot be free from; and the establishment of the concept is dependent on the absence of all benefits, so the concept is not established at all. It was said: Their intention is established; and the meaning of the speech is [valid] as long as no diverting factor from the benefits appears, so the possibility of other benefits is a possibility of diverting factors, and their possibility does not harm the apparent truth. But this is insufficient, for even if it is granted that their phrases avoid it, when the other benefits are realized the concept is not realized, because the truth is not realized when diverting factors exist, and the mentioned benefits are not absent from any speech, so no speech is free from a diverting factor from the truth, so it is never realized, so understand and do not slip, for it is a slippery place. (And) for us (thirdly: if the concept were established) it would be established in reports because the cause is the fear of lack of benefit) and it is common between them (and the consequent is false because if he said: 'In Syria, grazing sheep [only]' it would not indicate the absence of non-grazing sheep there (necessarily, and insisting on it is obstinacy. Likewise in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, it was said in the gloss: Despite being obstinacy, some have insisted on it, until al-Taftazani said: The truth is no difference between reports and commands. This [refutation] and the truth is that there is no obstinacy in it, for the meaning of this speech is not [that there is] no non-grazing sheep in Syria, but it is prevented by an external preventer like knowledge of the existence of non-grazing sheep there, and this is a diverting factor that does not harm the indication of the speech itself. Then if the claim of consensus on the non-existence of the concept in reports were valid, the discussion would be complete. (And it was answered: In a report, the absence of informing does not necessitate the absence) of the ruling (externally). The utmost is the lack of information about the status of the unmentioned, so the absence of the ruling externally is not necessitated, since informing has no role in the existence or non-existence of the ruling externally, unlike a legal ruling (established by command), for it has no external [existence]; so the obligation of zakat is his saying 'I oblige', so when the statement (which is the command) is absent, the obligation is absent because it is the establisher, and it has been absent in the unmentioned: the statement is absent, so the ruling is absent. Thus the difference between report and command becomes clear, so the necessary connection is denied. (Ibn al-Hajib said: This is subtle, and it was refuted by saying it is a statement negating the concept, and it is [merely] unmentioned, not that it is ruled by the opposite of the ruling, because its essence is non-exposure to the ruling (linguistically). Absence [of ruling] only follows from the absence of the establisher, and we also say that: it is a statement of leaving the unmentioned on the original principle, so understand, for it is very apparent. And he argued firstly: if the concept were established, then either by reason or transmission; reason has no role in establishing linguistic conventions, and transmission is either mutawatir in reality or in effect, or ahad. (There is no tawatur) here (in reality or in effect) such as consensus or like the inductive observation that the agent is raised [as nominative] unanimously between us and you. Also, if it were so, the leading scholars in induction and investigation would not have denied it, and ahad [reports] are not useful in such [matters] because all share in the cause of knowledge. Some insisted on tawatur, which is obstinacy, otherwise the convention would be certain, rather the indication would be certain in the absence of a diverting factor, as is the case with all real meanings, and this is contrary to consensus. (And it was answered): We do not accept that ahad reports are not useful; rather they are) useful for certainty by accepting ahad reports from al-Asma'i and al-Khalil for example) in the convention of words. (I say: Correct induction shows) that the existence of basic indication is certain in the typical structures of common constructions among ahad [reports] from commoners and elite. This is because everyone speaks with these constructions and conveys what is in his mind, and similarly understands when addressed, so everyone knows its meaning. Thus the cause of knowledge is common to all, unlike rarely used constructions, for they may not be certain nor known to all, but only to some, so in such [cases] ahad reports are not accepted at all; rather it is not unlikely to be certain that the single transmitter is mistaken. (And even if ahad are accepted in (partial materials because it is possible that one hears and another does not, yet the construction of the described and the attribute is common among all; so if it indicated a contrary ruling in the unmentioned, it would be certain and mutawatir, and ahad would not be accepted in it, so understand. Thus the required [conclusion] is established by the soundest proof that no doubt can refute. (It was said in the glosses of Mirzajan: The inference using this argument for negating the concept is incorrect, and it is said: Your proof for negation is either rational, which) reason (cannot independently [establish], or transmitted... i.e. either mutawatir in reality or effect, and it is not so, or ahad, and it is insufficient for such [matters]. This objection is a general refutation, and it can be formulated as a counter-argument: The statement negating the concept is false, for the proof upon it is either rational or transmitted... (I say: Our proof is rational along with definite transmitted [proof]. If it is assumed that there is no cause (for the convention except transmission via tawatur, then by its absence) i.e. lack of tawatur (its absence is necessarily known). And here it is certainly known that there is no tawatur in the transmission at all, so it is known that there is no indication at all, since its cause is only tawatur alone. This is not an independence of reason such that it is not accepted; rather it revolves around transmission, and it is not denied. (Reflect) for the truth does not go beyond it. (And) he argued (secondly: if the concept were valid) it would not be valid to say 'Give zakat for grazing [sheep] and for non-grazing [sheep]' neither together (i.e. in one sentence) nor separately (i.e. in two sentences), because then its weight would be like your saying: 'Do not say 'uff' to him' and 'Strike him' in being a combination of two contradictories. For his saying 'Give zakat for grazing [sheep]' indicates the non-obligation of zakat on non-grazing, and when non-grazing is conjoined, it indicates its obligation, just as 'Do not say 'uff' to him' prohibits hitting, and 'Strike him' commands it. (And it was answered: That is, the concept of opposition is not like the concept of agreement because of the certainty of that (i.e., concept of agreement) and the uncertainty of this (i.e., concept of opposition); the weak is nullified by the strong which is the explicit [text about] non-grazing, so there is no concept here because the strong prevents. But you can formulate the proof: if the concept were a meaning of the speech, the two contradictories would be understood in the mentioned example, even if one is left due to uncertainty, just as when two explicit texts conflict, one being uncertain, then the uncertain is left. But it is not so; rather the concept does not come to mind, so reflect on it. (And) he argued (thirdly: if the concept were established, there would be contradiction due to conflict between the concept and the explicit text or another concept frequently, as in the verse: {Do not consume usury, doubled and multiplied} (Al 'Imran: 130). For its concept [is that] consuming usury when it is not multiplied [is permissible], which contradicts the texts prohibiting even small amounts of usury. And that (i.e., contradiction) is contrary to the original principle; it is not resorted to except with proof, and there is no proof. If proof is brought, after its validity it would be a proof opposing your proof (due to the uncertainty of both), so they cancel each other, and the concept is not established. Perhaps by 'contradiction' he meant the prevention of their combination absolutely, for that suffices for the required [conclusion], not the contradiction in the sense of two equally strong proofs opposing each other, so that it would be argued that the existence of contradiction is not clear; the equality is obscure, so understand. (And it was answered) that it is refuted by the authoritative nature of ahad reports: if they were authoritative, contradiction would occur, because most ahad are contradictory; thus they are not resorted to except with proof, and if proof is brought it would oppose our proof, and they cancel each other, and the original is absence.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute over the validity of 'Mafhum al-Mukhalafa' (the concept of opposition) as a legal indicator. The author presents the Hanafi position that this concept is not a valid source of law, especially in commands (insha') as opposed to reports (ikhbar). The core argument is that the concept would require the absence of any other 'benefit' (fā'ida) in the speech, but every speech necessarily has such benefits, so the concept can never be established. Furthermore, in reports, the absence of mentioning a ruling does not imply its non-existence externally, unlike commands where the utterance itself creates the ruling. The author also refutes the claim that ahad reports can establish such a concept, arguing that the typical structures (like 'grazing sheep') are so common that their indication would have to be mutawatir, which it is not. The passage then presents and answers three counter-arguments: (1) that ahad reports can establish certainty in linguistic matters, answered by distinguishing partial materials from typical structures; (2) that if the concept were valid, one could not combine two different rulings (like zakat on grazing and non-grazing) without contradiction, answered by noting that the concept of opposition is weaker; (3) that it would create frequent contradictions with other texts, answered by analogy to ahad reports. The discussion ends with a refutation using the example of ahad reports: their authoritative nature itself leads to contradictions, so the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implied meaning that a ruling for the mentioned case implies the opposite ruling for the unmentioned case (e.g., 'grazing sheep require zakat' implies non-grazing do not).
مسكوت (maskut): The case that is not explicitly mentioned in the text, which is being considered for the concept.
صارف (sarif): A diverting factor that prevents the literal or real meaning from being taken, such as the presence of another benefit in the speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is mafhum al-mukhalafa not established?
A) It is never mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) Every speech contains a necessary benefit that diverts from the literal meaning, so the condition for the concept is never met.
C) It is rejected by ijma' of all scholars.
D) It only applies to commands, not reports.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-Mukhalafa cannot be a valid legal indicator because the necessary condition for its operation—absence of all other benefits in the description—is never fulfilled.

Mantuq and Mafhum
advanced
10 min
Refuting Counter-Arguments: The Hanafi Defense of Negating Mafhum al-Mukhalafa
Debate on whether Mafhum al-Mukhalafa is a valid legal indicator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain two key counter-arguments against the Hanafi negation of mafhum al-mukhalafa and articulate the Hanafi responses, including the distinction between partial and typical linguistic structures.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-Mukhalafa is not like Mafhum al-Muwafaqa; its uncertainty and potential for contradiction render it invalid.

This passage continues the debate on Mafhum al-Mukhalafa, presenting three counter-arguments from opposing scholars and the Hanafi responses. The author systematically refutes arguments that ahad reports can establish the concept, that it would cause contradictions in rulings, and that induction proves its certainty. Understanding these refutations solidifies the Hanafi position on the weakness of the concept of opposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first counter-argument and Hanafi response
Counter: Ahad reports from linguists (e.g., al-Asma'i) can establish certainty in linguistic conventions, so mafhum al-mukhalafa could be proven. Response: Ahad reports may work for isolated lexical items but not for typical syntactic structures like 'grazing sheep', which require tawatur.
Key phrase: 'الاستقراء الصحيح دل على أن وجود أصل الدلالة قطعي في الهيئات النوعية للتراكيب المتعارفة' (Correct induction shows that the basic indication is certain in typical structures).
2
Identify the second counter-argument and Hanafi response
Counter: If the concept were valid, one could not combine 'zakat on grazing' and 'zakat on non-grazing' without contradiction. Response: Mafhum al-Mukhalafa is weaker than Mafhum al-Muwafaqa; the stronger explicit text overrides the weaker concept.
The text compares to the contradiction between 'do not say uff' and 'strike him'—the explicit command overrides the implied prohibition.
3
Identify the third counter-argument and its refutation
Counter: The concept would cause frequent contradictions with other texts (e.g., the Quranic prohibition of usury with the concept allowing non-multiplied usury). Response: By analogy to ahad reports, contradiction does not invalidate the authoritative nature; the same reasoning applies here.
The refutation uses the example of ahad reports: their authoritative nature leads to contradictions, yet they are accepted; similarly, the concept is not established because the proof for negation stands.
4
Understand the final methodological point
The author concludes that the proof for negating the concept is 'the soundest proof that no doubt can refute' (أقوم حجة لا يدحضها شبهة), combining rational and transmitted evidence.

بالأصل أو تركه محلاً للاجتهاد والنظر بالقياس إلى المنطوق أو إلى غيره فائدة (لازمة لا يخلو الموصوف بالصفة عنها، وثبوت المفهوم متوقف على عدم الفوائد بأسرها فلا يثبت المفهوم أصلاً، قيل: مقصودهم ثابت؛ ومدلول للكلام ما لم يظهر صارف من الفوائد فاحتمال الفوائد الأخرى احتمال ،الصوارف واحتمالها لا يضر في الظن بالحقيقة وهذا غير واف فإنه لو سلم أن ذلك أن عباراتهم تنبو عنه، فالفوائد الأخرى إذا تحققت لم يتحقق المفهوم فإن الحقيقة لا تتحقق عند وجود الصوارف عنها، والفوائد المذكورة لا يخلو كلام ما عن واحد منها، فلا يخلو كلام ما عن الصارف عن الحقيقة، فلا تتحقق أصلاً فافهم ولا تزل فإنه مزلة (و) لنا (ثالثاً : لو ثبت) المفهوم الثبت في الخبر لأن العلة الحذر عن عدم الفائدة) وهو مشترك بينهما (والتالي باطل لأنه لو قال في الشام الغنم السائمة لم يدل على عدم المعلوفة فيها (ضرورة والتزامه مكابرة، كذا في شرح المختصر » قال في الحاشية» مع كونه مكابرة قد التزمه بعضهم حتى قال التفتازاني : والحق عدم الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، هذا والحق أنه لا مكابرة فيه، فإن مدلول هذا الكلام ليس في الشام المعلوفة، إلا أنه يمنع عنه مانع خارجي كالعلم بوجود المعلوفة فيه، وهذا صارف لا يضر في دلالة نفس الكلام ثم ادعاء الإجماع على عدم المفهوم في الخبر لو صح تم الكلام (وأجيب بأن في الخبر لا يلزم من عدم الإخبار العدم) للحكم (خارجاً) وغاية ما فيه عدم الإخبار عن حال المسكوت فلا يلزم عدم الحكم فيه في الخارج، إذ لا دخل للإخبار في ثبوت الحكم أو انتفائه في الخارج بخلاف الحكم الشرعي) الثابت الإنشاء فإنه لا خارج له فوجوب الزكاة هو قوله : أوجبت فإذا انتفى القول) الذي هو الإنشاء انتفى الوجوب لأنه هو المثبت وقد انتفى في المسكوت :القول فانتفى الحكم فاتضح الفرق بين الخبر والإنشاء، فالملازمة ممنوعة (قال ابن الحاجب هذا دقيق، ورد بأنه قول بنفي المفهوم وكونه مسكوت عنه لا كونه محكوماً بنقيض الحكم لأن حاصله عدم التعرض للحكم (لغة) وإنما يلزم الانتفاء لانتفاء المثبت وبه نقول أيضاً، فإنه قول ببقاء المسكوت على الأصل فافهم فإنه ظاهر جداً واستدل أولاً بأنه لو ثبت المفهوم فإما بالعقل أو النقل والعقل لا مدخل له في إثبات الأوضاع والنقل إما بالتواتر حقيقة أو حكماً أو بالآحاد (ولا تواتر) ههنا (حقيقة أو حكماً كالإجماع أو كاستقراء رفع الفاعل اتفاقاً بيننا وبينكم وأيضاً لو كان كذلك لم ينكره الأئمة ذوو اليد الطولى في الاستقراء والتتبع والآحاد لا تفيد في مثله لاشتراك الكل في سبب العلم، والتزم بعضهم التواتر وهو مكابرة، وإلا فكان الوضع مقطوعاً، بل تكون الدلالة عليه مقطوعة عند عدم الصارف كما هو شأن سائر الحقائق، وهذا خلاف الإجماع (وأجيب) لا نسلم أن الآحاد لا تفيد بل) تفيد للقطع بقبول الآحاد عن الأصمعي والخليل مثلا) في وضع الألفاظ (أقول : الاستقراء الصحيح دل) على أن وجود أصل الدلالة قطعي في الهيئات النوعية للتراكيب المتعارفة عند الآحاد من العوام والخواص، وهذا لأن كل أحد يتكلم بهذه التركيبات ويفيد بها ما في ضميره، وكذا يستفيد بها إذا خوطب فيعلم كل أحد معناه، فسبب العلم مشترك بين الكل بخلاف التراكيب القليلة الاستعمال، فإنه يجوز أن لا تكون قطعية ولا معلومة عند الكل، بل عند البعض فقط ففي مثله لا تقبل الآحاد البتة بل لا يبعد أن يقطع بخطأ الواحد الناقل (وإن قبل في (المواد الجزئية لجواز سماع واحد دون آخر وتركيب الموصوف والصفة متعارف عند الكل فلو كان دالاً على الحكم المخالف في المسكوت لكان قطعياً متواتراً ولا تقبل فيه الآحاد فافهم، فقد ثبت المطلوب بأقوم حجة لا يدحضها شبهة (قيل) في حواشي مرزاجان: الاستدلال بهذا الوجه على نفي المفهوم غير صحيح، ويقال : دليلكم على النفي إما عقلي وهو) أي العقل (لا يستقل أو نقلي إلى آخره أي فإما متواتر حقيقة أو حكماً وليس كذلك، أو أحادي، ولا يكفي في مثل هذا، وهذا الإيراد نقض إجمالي ويمكن أن يحرر معارضة بأن القول بنفي المفهوم باطل، فإن الدليل المقام عليه عقلي أو نقلي الخ... (أقول) دليلنا عقلي مع نقلي قاطع و إذا فرض أن لا علة (له أي للوضع إلا النقل تواتراً فبعدمه) أي التواتر (يعلم عدمه بالضرورة) وههنا معلوم قطعاً أن لا تواتر في النقل البتة، فيعلم أن لا دلالة أصلاً، إذ علتها ليست إلا التواتر فحسب وهذا ليس باستقلال للعقل حتى لا يقبل بل دوران مع النقل) وهو غير منكر (تدبر) فإنه لا يتجاوز عنه الحق (و) استدل (ثانياً لو صح) المفهوم (لما صح أذ زكاة السائمة والمعلوفة لا مجتمعاً أي في جملة (ولا متفرقاً) أي في جملتين لأن وزانه حينئذٍ وزان) قولك: لا تقل له أف (واضربه في كونه جمعاً بين متنافيين، فإن قوله أد زكاة السائمة يدل على عدم وجوب زكاة المعلوفة، وإذا عطف المعلوفة دل على وجوبها، كما أن لا تقل له أف يقتضي النهي عن الضرب واضربه أمر به (وأجيب بأنه) أي مفهوم المخالفة (ليس كمفهوم الموافقة لقطعية ذلك أي مفهوم الموافقة (وظنية هذا) أي مفهوم المخالفة ويضمحل الضعيف مع القوي الذي هو منطوق والمعلوفة فليس ههنا مفهوم لمنع القوي ولك أن تقرر الدليل بأنه لو كان المفهوم مدلولاً للكلام لفهم المتنافيان في المثال المذكور وإن كان يترك أحدهما للظنية كما يفهم المتنافيان فيما إذا تعارض المنطوقان أحدهما ظني ثم يترك الظني، وليس الأمر كذلك، بل لا يحضر المفهوم بالبال فليتأمل فيه (و) استدل (ثالثاً : لو ثبت المفهوم الثبت التعارض لثبوت المخالفة بين المفهوم والمنطوق أو المفهوم الآخر كثيراً كقوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبوا أَضْعَفًا مُضَعَفَةٌ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٠] ) فإن مفهومه أكل الربا إذا لم يكن أضعافاً، وهو مخالف للنصوص المحرمة للربا القليل أيضاً (وهو) أي التعارض (خلاف الأصل لا يصار إليه إلا بدليل ولا دليل فإن أقيم فبعد صحته كان دليلاً معارضاً لدليلكم (لظنيتهما) فيتساقطان فلا يثبت المفهوم، ولعله أراد بالتعارض التخالف المانع اجتماعهما مطلقاً، فإنه يكفي في المطلوب لا التعارض بمعنى تقاوم الحجتين المتساويتين في القوة حتى يرد أن وجود التعارض كثيراً غير بين فالتعادل في حيز الخفاء فافهم (وأجيب) بأنه (منقوض بحجية خبر الواحد فإنه لو كان حجة لوقع التعارض، لأن أكثر الآحاد متعارضة فلا يصار إليه إلا بالدليل، وإن أقيم يكون معارضاً لدليلنا فيتساقطان والأصل عدم
Their intention with Fawatih al-Rahamut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut Part One: The subject or its attributes cannot be separated from structure, so the existence of a diverting factor is necessary; thus there is no indication of the negation of the ruling at all, so reflect. (And) for us (secondly: leaving the unmentioned as a place for inference by the original principle, or leaving it as a place for ijtihad and consideration by analogy to the explicit or to other [texts] is a necessary benefit that the described [thing] cannot be free from; and the establishment of the concept is dependent on the absence of all benefits, so the concept is not established at all. It was said: Their intention is established; and the meaning of the speech is [valid] as long as no diverting factor from the benefits appears, so the possibility of other benefits is a possibility of diverting factors, and their possibility does not harm the apparent truth. But this is insufficient, for even if it is granted that their phrases avoid it, when the other benefits are realized the concept is not realized, because the truth is not realized when diverting factors exist, and the mentioned benefits are not absent from any speech, so no speech is free from a diverting factor from the truth, so it is never realized, so understand and do not slip, for it is a slippery place. (And) for us (thirdly: if the concept were established) it would be established in reports because the cause is the fear of lack of benefit) and it is common between them (and the consequent is false because if he said: 'In Syria, grazing sheep [only]' it would not indicate the absence of non-grazing sheep there (necessarily, and insisting on it is obstinacy. Likewise in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, it was said in the gloss: Despite being obstinacy, some have insisted on it, until al-Taftazani said: The truth is no difference between reports and commands. This [refutation] and the truth is that there is no obstinacy in it, for the meaning of this speech is not [that there is] no non-grazing sheep in Syria, but it is prevented by an external preventer like knowledge of the existence of non-grazing sheep there, and this is a diverting factor that does not harm the indication of the speech itself. Then if the claim of consensus on the non-existence of the concept in reports were valid, the discussion would be complete. (And it was answered: In a report, the absence of informing does not necessitate the absence) of the ruling (externally). The utmost is the lack of information about the status of the unmentioned, so the absence of the ruling externally is not necessitated, since informing has no role in the existence or non-existence of the ruling externally, unlike a legal ruling (established by command), for it has no external [existence]; so the obligation of zakat is his saying 'I oblige', so when the statement (which is the command) is absent, the obligation is absent because it is the establisher, and it has been absent in the unmentioned: the statement is absent, so the ruling is absent. Thus the difference between report and command becomes clear, so the necessary connection is denied. (Ibn al-Hajib said: This is subtle, and it was refuted by saying it is a statement negating the concept, and it is [merely] unmentioned, not that it is ruled by the opposite of the ruling, because its essence is non-exposure to the ruling (linguistically). Absence [of ruling] only follows from the absence of the establisher, and we also say that: it is a statement of leaving the unmentioned on the original principle, so understand, for it is very apparent. And he argued firstly: if the concept were established, then either by reason or transmission; reason has no role in establishing linguistic conventions, and transmission is either mutawatir in reality or in effect, or ahad. (There is no tawatur) here (in reality or in effect) such as consensus or like the inductive observation that the agent is raised [as nominative] unanimously between us and you. Also, if it were so, the leading scholars in induction and investigation would not have denied it, and ahad [reports] are not useful in such [matters] because all share in the cause of knowledge. Some insisted on tawatur, which is obstinacy, otherwise the convention would be certain, rather the indication would be certain in the absence of a diverting factor, as is the case with all real meanings, and this is contrary to consensus. (And it was answered): We do not accept that ahad reports are not useful; rather they are) useful for certainty by accepting ahad reports from al-Asma'i and al-Khalil for example) in the convention of words. (I say: Correct induction shows) that the existence of basic indication is certain in the typical structures of common constructions among ahad [reports] from commoners and elite. This is because everyone speaks with these constructions and conveys what is in his mind, and similarly understands when addressed, so everyone knows its meaning. Thus the cause of knowledge is common to all, unlike rarely used constructions, for they may not be certain nor known to all, but only to some, so in such [cases] ahad reports are not accepted at all; rather it is not unlikely to be certain that the single transmitter is mistaken. (And even if ahad are accepted in (partial materials because it is possible that one hears and another does not, yet the construction of the described and the attribute is common among all; so if it indicated a contrary ruling in the unmentioned, it would be certain and mutawatir, and ahad would not be accepted in it, so understand. Thus the required [conclusion] is established by the soundest proof that no doubt can refute. (It was said in the glosses of Mirzajan: The inference using this argument for negating the concept is incorrect, and it is said: Your proof for negation is either rational, which) reason (cannot independently [establish], or transmitted... i.e. either mutawatir in reality or effect, and it is not so, or ahad, and it is insufficient for such [matters]. This objection is a general refutation, and it can be formulated as a counter-argument: The statement negating the concept is false, for the proof upon it is either rational or transmitted... (I say: Our proof is rational along with definite transmitted [proof]. If it is assumed that there is no cause (for the convention except transmission via tawatur, then by its absence) i.e. lack of tawatur (its absence is necessarily known). And here it is certainly known that there is no tawatur in the transmission at all, so it is known that there is no indication at all, since its cause is only tawatur alone. This is not an independence of reason such that it is not accepted; rather it revolves around transmission, and it is not denied. (Reflect) for the truth does not go beyond it. (And) he argued (secondly: if the concept were valid) it would not be valid to say 'Give zakat for grazing [sheep] and for non-grazing [sheep]' neither together (i.e. in one sentence) nor separately (i.e. in two sentences), because then its weight would be like your saying: 'Do not say 'uff' to him' and 'Strike him' in being a combination of two contradictories. For his saying 'Give zakat for grazing [sheep]' indicates the non-obligation of zakat on non-grazing, and when non-grazing is conjoined, it indicates its obligation, just as 'Do not say 'uff' to him' prohibits hitting, and 'Strike him' commands it. (And it was answered: That is, the concept of opposition is not like the concept of agreement because of the certainty of that (i.e., concept of agreement) and the uncertainty of this (i.e., concept of opposition); the weak is nullified by the strong which is the explicit [text about] non-grazing, so there is no concept here because the strong prevents. But you can formulate the proof: if the concept were a meaning of the speech, the two contradictories would be understood in the mentioned example, even if one is left due to uncertainty, just as when two explicit texts conflict, one being uncertain, then the uncertain is left. But it is not so; rather the concept does not come to mind, so reflect on it. (And) he argued (thirdly: if the concept were established, there would be contradiction due to conflict between the concept and the explicit text or another concept frequently, as in the verse: {Do not consume usury, doubled and multiplied} (Al 'Imran: 130). For its concept [is that] consuming usury when it is not multiplied [is permissible], which contradicts the texts prohibiting even small amounts of usury. And that (i.e., contradiction) is contrary to the original principle; it is not resorted to except with proof, and there is no proof. If proof is brought, after its validity it would be a proof opposing your proof (due to the uncertainty of both), so they cancel each other, and the concept is not established. Perhaps by 'contradiction' he meant the prevention of their combination absolutely, for that suffices for the required [conclusion], not the contradiction in the sense of two equally strong proofs opposing each other, so that it would be argued that the existence of contradiction is not clear; the equality is obscure, so understand. (And it was answered) that it is refuted by the authoritative nature of ahad reports: if they were authoritative, contradiction would occur, because most ahad are contradictory; thus they are not resorted to except with proof, and if proof is brought it would oppose our proof, and they cancel each other, and the original is absence.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute over the validity of 'Mafhum al-Mukhalafa' (the concept of opposition) as a legal indicator. The author presents the Hanafi position that this concept is not a valid source of law, especially in commands (insha') as opposed to reports (ikhbar). The core argument is that the concept would require the absence of any other 'benefit' (fā'ida) in the speech, but every speech necessarily has such benefits, so the concept can never be established. Furthermore, in reports, the absence of mentioning a ruling does not imply its non-existence externally, unlike commands where the utterance itself creates the ruling. The author also refutes the claim that ahad reports can establish such a concept, arguing that the typical structures (like 'grazing sheep') are so common that their indication would have to be mutawatir, which it is not. The passage then presents and answers three counter-arguments: (1) that ahad reports can establish certainty in linguistic matters, answered by distinguishing partial materials from typical structures; (2) that if the concept were valid, one could not combine two different rulings (like zakat on grazing and non-grazing) without contradiction, answered by noting that the concept of opposition is weaker; (3) that it would create frequent contradictions with other texts, answered by analogy to ahad reports. The discussion ends with a refutation using the example of ahad reports: their authoritative nature itself leads to contradictions, so the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implied meaning that a ruling for the mentioned case implies the opposite ruling for the unmentioned case.
مسكوت (maskut): The case that is not explicitly mentioned in the text.
صارف (sarif): A diverting factor that prevents the literal meaning from being taken.
هيئات نوعية (hay'at naw'iyya): Typical syntactic structures that are common in the language, such as the construction of described and attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Hanafi author reject the argument that ahad reports from linguists can establish the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa?
A) Ahad reports are never accepted in any linguistic matter.
B) The typical syntactic structures involved are too common to be established by ahad, requiring tawatur.
C) The linguists cited are not reliable transmitters.
D) The concept is rejected by ijma'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school refutes counter-arguments against rejecting mafhum al-mukhalafa by distinguishing between lexical and syntactic structures, emphasizing that the concept is too weak to be a binding indicator.

Mantuq and Mafhum
intermediate
6 min
Mafhum Is Not Among the Three Significations
Arguing that mafhum does not fall under the three significations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies mafhum outside the three primary significations (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Mafhum is a conventional implication, not a rational one, so it falls outside the three primary significations.

This passage tackles a subtle point in Hanafi usul: where does mafhum (implicit meaning) fit among the established categories of linguistic signification? The Hanafi position argues that mafhum does not belong to mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam as traditionally defined. Let's trace the reasoning and see how the Shafi'i view is rebutted.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on mafhum
Identify whether the Hanafi school considers mafhum part of the three significations or not.
The Hanafi view is that mafhum is a separate category of conventional implication (luzum 'urfi), not included in mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam as defined by the early scholars.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which school or scholar claims that mafhum is included in one of the three significations.
The Shafi'i author of al-Minhaj considers mafhum as iltizam, while some other Shafi'is claim it is mutabaqa (systematic assignment).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning behind the opponent's classification of mafhum.
They argue that mafhum is iltizam because the unmentioned meaning is necessarily implied by the wording, or that it is mutabaqa because it is a type of systematic assignment for the composition.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts the opponent's proof.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between rational (luzum 'aqli) and conventional (luzum 'urfi) implication, showing that mafhum is only conventional and therefore not iltizam as traditionally understood. They also criticize the Shafi'i position as inconsistent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this disagreement in fiqh rulings.
The Hanafi school does not accept mafhum al-mukhalafah as a binding proof unless supported by other indicators, whereas some Shafi'is accept it based on the wording alone.

له، التكليف فيبقى عليه (و) أجيب أيضاً بأنه منقوض بترجيح بينة الخارج) مع بينة ذي اليد مع أنهما يتعارضان فيتساقطان ويبقى المدعي في يد ذي اليد على الأصل، والحل أن بعد قيام الدليل يعدل عن مقتضى الأصل فتدبر) هذا والجواب أنه فرق بين ما نحن فيه وصورتي النقض، فإنه لم يفهم ههنا دليل خال عن الدخل حتى يعدل لأجله عن مقتضى الأصل، بخلاف حجية خبر الواحد فإنها ثابتة بدليل قاطع لا مرد له فيخرج عن قاعدة الأصل، وأما بينة الخارج فلا يعارضها بينة ذي اليد، بل بينة لا تثبت شيئاً فوق ما تثبته اليد فلا تعارض حتى يتساقطا، ولهذا تساقط بينتاهما إذا كانت بينة ذي اليد على النتاج لوجود التعارض وترك المدعي في يد ذي اليد كما عند بعض المشايخ، أو يرجح باليد فيقضي له كما هو المختار، فافهم وبه اندفع الحل أيضاً فليتأمل فيه (و) استدل (رابعاً) بأن المفهوم ولو كان لكان داخلاً في واحد من المطابقة والتضمن والإلتزام و ليست بإحدى الدلالات الثلاث وأجيب بأنه وضع نوعي للتركيب فيكون مطابقة ولا يكون (منطوقاً لأنها ليست على المذكور (وفي المنهاج للتزام الالتزام لأن المسكوت غير الموضوع له وهو بعيد عن الإفادة لأنهم عدوا الالتزام من أقسام المنطوق وجوابه أنه كما روينا سابقاً أن بعض الشافعية ومنهم صاحب المنهاج لم يعدوا الالتزام من المنطوق (و) هو بعيد عن (التمام) أيضاً، لأن النفي عن المسكوت ليس لازماً ذهنياً، وإنما ذلك لو شرط في الدلالة اللزوم العقلي حتى لا تكون دلالة حاتم على الجود حين استعمل یرد في معناه التزاماً وهو بعيد من هذا الفن بل الالتزام ما ينتقل الذهن إليه، سواء كان لازماً ذهنياً أو عرفياً، ويفهم بعد التأمل كما مر في أمثلة الإشارة الخفية والمفهوم لازم عرفي إن لم يكن هناك فائدة أخرى، ولا يحسن حمل الالتزام على التزام أهل العربية فإنه مجاز، والمنطوق حقيقة، فيلزم الجمع إلا أن صاحب المنهاج يجيزه فافهم، وقد دريت أن كلام الشافعية مضطرب في المفهوم فتارة يدعون كونه موضوعاً له وتارة كونه معنى التزامياً، فافهم،
He said: The taklif remains upon him. And it was answered also that it is contradicted by giving preponderance to the external evidence over the evidence of the possessor, while they conflict and cancel each other out, and the claimant remains in the hand of the possessor based on the original presumption. The solution is that after the evidence is established, one deviates from the requirement of the original principle, so reflect. This and the answer is that there is a difference between our case and the two cases of objection. For in this case no evidence free from defect is understood to deviate for its sake from the requirement of the original principle, unlike the authority of isolated reports (khabar al-wahid) which is established by decisive proof that cannot be rejected, so it exits from the rule of the original principle. As for the external evidence, it is not opposed by the evidence of the possessor, but rather evidence that does not prove anything beyond what the hand proves does not conflict such that they cancel each other out. For this reason their two pieces of evidence cancel out if the possessor's evidence is about offspring due to the existence of conflict, and the claimant is left in the hand of the possessor as according to some mashayikh, or he is given preponderance by possession and judgment is given for him as is the chosen view. So understand, and with this the solution is also repelled, so let it be pondered. And (fourthly) it was argued: the concept (mafhum), if it were, would be included in one of correspondence (mutabaqa), inclusion (tadammun), or implication (iltizam), and it is not among the three significations. And it was answered: it is a type of systematic assignment (wad' naw'i) for the composition, so it is mutabaqa, and it is not mantuq (explicit speech) because it is not about the mentioned. In al-Minhaj, it is considered iltizam because the unmentioned is not the subject of the wording, and that is far from benefit because they counted iltizam as a part of mantuq. And its answer: as we narrated previously, some Shafi'is including the author of al-Minhaj did not count iltizam as mantuq. And it is also far from completion, because the negation regarding the unmentioned is not a mental necessary implication; that would only be if mental necessity were stipulated in signification, so that the signification of Hatim's generosity when used in its meaning would not be iltizam, and that is far from this discipline. Rather, iltizam is what the mind moves to, whether mentally necessary or conventionally necessary, and it is understood after reflection as mentioned in the examples of subtle indication (ishara khafiyya). And the concept is a conventional necessary implication if there is no other benefit. And it is not good to restrict iltizam to the iltizam of the Arabs, for it is metaphorical, while mantuq is literal, so the combination is necessary, except that the author of al-Minhaj permits it, so understand. And you have known that the speech of the Shafi'is is confused regarding the concept: sometimes they claim it is the subject of wording and sometimes it is an iltizam meaning, so understand.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument (رابعاً) in the dispute over the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafah. The argument states that if mafhum were a valid signification, it would have to be included under one of the three established categories of signification: mutabaqa (correspondence), tadammun (inclusion), or iltizam (implication). However, mafhum does not fit into any of these. The response from the proponents is that mafhum is a systematic assignment (wad' naw'i) of the composition, thus it is mutabaqa. The text then contrasts this with the view of the author of al-Minhaj (a Shafi'i work) who considers mafhum as iltizam. The Hanafi author rebuts that this iltizam is not the mental necessary implication (luzum 'aqli) but rather a conventional implication (luzum 'urfi), which is a different category. He criticizes the Shafi'i position as inconsistent. The lesson illustrates the subtle distinctions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the classification of linguistic significations, and how the Hanafi school requires a precise understanding of 'iltizam' that distinguishes between rational and conventional implications.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The implied meaning understood from the context, not explicitly stated, particularly the opposite implication (mafhum al-mukhalafah).
المنطوق (al-mantuq): The explicit meaning stated directly by the wording.
المطابقة (al-mutabaqa): The correspondence between a word and its complete, literal meaning.
التضمن (al-tadammun): The inclusion of a part of the meaning within the whole.
الالتزام (al-iltizam): The necessary implication that the mind moves to, whether rational or conventional, from the wording to something not directly stated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument against including mafhum among the three significations (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam)?
A) Mafhum is not based on the wording at all.
B) Mafhum does not fit into any of the three categories as defined.
C) Mafhum is only valid in the Shafi'i school.
D) The three significations are rejected by Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum is not part of the three primary significations; it is a conventional implication that requires additional evidence to be a binding proof in fiqh.

Mantuq and Mafhum
intermediate
12 min
The Scholar Understanding Argument for Mafhum al-Mukhalafah
Proponents cite Abu Ubayd and al-Shafi'i's understanding; opponents counter with al-Akhfash and Imam Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument from scholar understanding regarding mafhum al-sifah.

Core Idea
Expert understanding does not establish mafhum if it can be explained by cause ('illa); only linguistic principles qualify.

This lesson explores one of the key arguments used by proponents of mafhum al-mukhalafah: the appeal to the understanding of expert Arab linguists and jurists like Abu Ubayd and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi school responds by showing that their understanding was based on the underlying cause ('illa) of the ruling, not on a purely linguistic implication, and that earlier authorities like al-Akhfash and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly denied mafhum al-sifah. This debate illustrates the fundamental difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i approaches to text and inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i argument from scholar understanding
State the claim: Abu Ubayd and al-Shafi'i understood from two hadiths that the absence of a description (wajid/ghani) negates the ruling. This is presented as proof that mafhum al-sifah is valid.
2
Examine the Hanafi first response: cause-based explanation
The Hanafi rebuttal argues that the understanding is not due to linguistic implication but to the underlying cause ('illa). The ruling is tied to solvency or wealth as a cause; when the cause is absent, the ruling is negated by logical inference, not by the description itself.
3
Examine the Hanafi second response: counter-authorities and chronological preference
The Hanafis cite al-Akhfash (three linguists) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who explicitly denied mafhum al-sifah. Since they are earlier and possess purer Arabic, their view is preferred over later scholars like al-Shafi'i and Abu Ubayd.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: In fiqh, Hanafis do not accept mafhum al-sifah as a binding proof, so they may derive different rulings from the same hadith compared to Shafi'is, who rely on such implications.
5
Evaluate the overall tarjih
The text ultimately gives preference to the Hanafi position by showing that the Shafi'i proof is not definitive: understanding alone is not a universal rule, and the counter-authorities are stronger both in time and in explicit denial.

The affirmers of the concept (mafhum) said: First: it is authentically reported from Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam – and this is the well-known one, and in al-Bada'i‘: Abu Ubayda (with the feminine-ending tāʼ) i.e. Ma‘mar ibn al-Muthannā. It is said that Imam al-Haramayn clearly stated it, and he said in Sharh al-Sharh: the correct view is what the Imam said. And it was said there is no contradiction because both understandings are possible. The Imam transmitted from one and in the well-known view from the other his understanding from his statement (peace be upon him): 'The procrastination of the solvent makes his honor and punishment permissible.' This was narrated by Ahmad, and he understood from it that the procrastination of the non-solvent does not make his honor and punishment permissible. And likewise, his understanding from his statement (peace be upon him): 'The procrastination of the rich is oppression' is that the procrastination of the non-rich is not oppression. And similarly from al-Shafi‘i his understanding is authentically reported. And both are imams, knowledgeable in language, so their view is authoritative. The first answer: understanding is not a universal rule. Perhaps his understanding from them in this particular partial example does not validate because the description indicates causation, and the principle is that there is no other cause. So the cause for the permissibility of punishment is solvency, and likewise the cause of oppression is wealth. So by its absence the ruling is negated, and this is not due to language. You may say: harming a Muslim was prohibited by decisive texts such as the hadith: 'The Muslim is the one from whose tongue and hand the Muslims are safe' (agreed upon). Harm was only permitted in the case of the indebted solvent to repel his oppression and obtain the right, and in other cases there is no oppression from him. [PAGE_455] The third treatise on linguistic principles: because of lack of transgression and no access to the right, it remains on the original prohibition. And it is known from this principle that the specification of the solvent and the rich is because the poor person's ruling is opposite, not because the description indicates the negation of this ruling. However, the followers of Imam al-Shafi‘i transmitted from him his understanding of the concept due to the description, so these points do not apply to his understanding. As for the statement of Abu Ubayd when it was said to him: the intended meaning of the hadith 'For a stomach of one of you to be filled with pus is better for him than to be filled with poetry' is the condemnation of poets and the satire of the Prophet (peace be upon him) against them; if it were so, the mention of 'filling' would be devoid of meaning, because a little of it is likewise. So this also does not indicate his understanding of the concept. Rather, perhaps his purpose is that condemnation is for the filling, while regarding the little, it is passed over in silence and remains on the original permissibility. And if the purpose were condemnation absolutely, not condemnation of much and silence about little, the mentioned would be pointless. And the statement that it is a mere possibility does not undermine the argument because the apparent is their understanding from the description. This is denied: how can it be? And the existence of the possibility of difference disqualifies the proof from being authority, and the appearance of understanding from the description is denied; there must be evidence. And the second answer: it is countered by what is authentically reported from al-Akhfash – from the three: Abu al-Khattab ‘Abd al-Hamid ibn ‘Abd al-Majid, the teacher of Sibawayh; Abu al-Hasan Sa‘id ibn Mas‘ada, the companion of Sibawayh; and Abu al-Hasan ‘Ali ibn Sulayman, the companion of Tha‘lab and al-Mubarrad – each of them is an imam in language, as in the margin. And the apparent is that it is the companion of Sibawayh, because he is the one intended by the absolute term, it is said. And (also) Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, that there is no concept for the description. And both are imams in Arabic. Imam Muhammad said: my father left me thirty thousand dirhams, and I spent half of them on grammar and poetry and half on hadith and fiqh. This indicates his seriousness and complete effort in acquiring the Arabic sciences. So if the statement of such two imams is conflicting, then there is no proof in their understanding. And even if one claims natural aptitude (saliqa) in Abu Ubayd and al-Shafi‘i (may Allah be pleased with them) or great knowledge of Arabic and strength of reliable transmission from them, then al-Shaybani is the imam in natural aptitude and knowledge, and the transmission from him is strong, more authentic, and mass-transmitted due to the abundance of his followers. Rather, Imam al-Shaybani has precedence in time over them. For Imam Muhammad was born in the year 132 AH and died in 189 AH. Al-Shafi‘i was born in 150 AH, which is the year of death of the great Imam Abu Hanifa, as transmitted by reliable sources. And the author transmitted from al-Taqrir that he was born in 152 AH and died in 204 AH. And Abu Ubayd died in 224 AH at the age of 67 or 73, as in al-Taysir. And in the history of Ibn Khallakan, al-Bukhari said it, and it was said 222 AH, and said 223 AH. And Abu Ubayda Ma‘mar died in 209 or 211 or 213 AH. Then if Abu Ubayda is Ma‘mar as transmitted from Imam al-Haramayn, what relation does he have to Imam Muhammad? For he was attributed to exiting the religion (al-khuruj), Allah forbid. And in the history of Ibn Khallakan, he held the doctrine of the Khawarij, and there was no one on the face of the earth more knowledgeable among the Khawarij than him. As for Imam Muhammad, he is an imam in piety and a vessel of knowledge, so understand. And there is no doubt for anyone that precedence belongs to the earlier due to the lack of mixing of the Arabic language in the earlier period. And the Companions were self-sufficient from composing works on grammar and morphology. And some Hanafis transmitted the discipleship of al-Shafi‘i to him, and some Shafi‘is strongly denied it. And Ibn Taymiyya said: what is authentically established is his debate with him. Similarly in.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument of the affirmers of mafhum al-mukhalafah (opposite implication). They cite the authentic understanding of two renowned linguists and jurists: Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam and Imam al-Shafi‘i. Both understood from two hadiths—'The procrastination of the solvent makes his honor and punishment permissible' and 'The procrastination of the rich is oppression'—that the opposite rulings apply when the descriptions (solvent and rich) are absent. The affirmers argue that if such expert linguists understood the concept from these descriptions, then it validates mafhum al-sifah. The Hanafi response is twofold. First, this understanding is not based on linguistic implication but on the underlying cause ('illa): the ruling of permissibility is tied to solvency as a cause, and similarly oppression is tied to wealth. When the cause is absent, the ruling is negated by logical inference, not by the description itself. Second, they cite counter-authorities: al-Akhfash and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, both imams in Arabic, who explicitly denied the concept of the description. The text then stresses the superiority of Imam Muhammad in terms of time (born earlier) and knowledge of pure Arabic from the early period. The lesson clarifies that mere understanding by scholars is not a definitive proof; it must be supported by linguistic principles or other evidence. The chronological argument—that earlier scholars have purer understanding of Arabic—favors the Hanafi position which rejects mafhum al-sifah.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The implied meaning derived from the description (wasf), where the presence of the description indicates the ruling and its absence indicates the opposite.
الوصف (al-wasf): The description or attribute in the text (e.g., 'wajid' or 'ghani') from which the concept is derived.
السليقة (al-saliqa): Natural linguistic aptitude, an innate ability to understand Arabic, claimed for the affirmers of mafhum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi response to the argument that Abu Ubayd and al-Shafi‘i understood mafhum from the hadith?
A) Their understanding is rejected because they were not linguists.
B) The understanding is based on the underlying cause ('illa), not the linguistic description.
C) The hadiths are inauthentic, so their understanding is irrelevant.
D) The concept is only valid in the Shafi‘i school, so it does not affect Hanafi fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Expert understanding of a text does not constitute proof for mafhum al-mukhalafah if it can be explained by the underlying cause; the Hanafi position is that such understanding is not a linguistic principle but an inference from cause.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Mafhum al-Shart: The Hanafi Rejection of Conditional Inference
Usul dispute on validity of mafhum al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects mafhum al-shart as a valid legal proof and evaluate the counterarguments from its proponents.

Core Idea
Negation of a condition does not necessitate negation of the ruling — mafhum al-shart is linguistically and rationally unsound.

In usul al-fiqh, one of the key debates is whether the concept of condition (mafhum al-shart) constitutes a valid proof for deriving legal rulings. While some schools and even a few Hanafi scholars like Imam al-Karkhi affirm it, the dominant Hanafi position firmly rejects it. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut lays out the Hanafi evidence, refuting the linguistic and causal arguments of the proponents. Mastering this dispute sharpens your understanding of how Hanafis prioritize explicit textual evidence over implied logical structures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested concept
Define mafhum al-shart as the idea that negating a condition negates the ruling. Note that it is similar to mafhum al-sifa and that some Hanafis like al-Karkhi affirm it.
The passage explicitly states that mafhum al-shart is like mafhum al-sifa and that some affirm it.
2
State the Hanafi position and primary proof
The Hanafi position is that removal of the antecedent does not entail removal of the consequent. The rational and customary proof is that conditional particles are used even when the antecedent is more specific, which would be impossible if mafhum were valid.
The verse 24:33 is cited as an example where the condition does not imply permission when absent.
3
Examine the proponents' linguistic argument
Proponents compare the conditional particle 'in' to 'law', claiming that both indicate negation of the consequence upon negation of the condition.
They argue the linguistic structure itself indicates negation upon negation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the linguistic argument
Hanafis respond that if mafhum were true, conditional particles could not be used when the antecedent is more specific or general, but they are. This disproves the necessity of mafhum.
The author calls this 'ugliness' (shanā‘ah) and says no one should adhere to it.
5
Examine and rebut the causal argument
Proponents shift to a causal argument, claiming that 'an' is predominantly used for causation, so absence of cause negates effect. Hanafis counter that 'an' is also used for concomitance and correlation, not just causation, and even if causal, it is not a linguistic indication for a legal ruling.
The passage concludes that the causal argument is insufficient for a legal proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها مفهوم الشرط) وهو انتفاء الحكم عند انتفاء الشرط وهو كالصفة) أي مفهوم الشرط كمفهوم الصفة (وقيل) هو (أقوى) منه، وقال به جميع من قال بمفهوم الصفة وبعض من لم يقل به كالشيخ الإمام أبي الحسن الكرخي من مشايخنا لنا ما تقرر) عقلاً وعرفاً (أن رفع المقدم لا يدل على رفع التالي، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُكْرِهُوا فَنَيَاتِكُمْ عَلَى الْبِغَاءِ إِنْ أَرَدْنَ تَحَصُّنًا﴾ [النور: 33] (الآية) واعترض عليه بأن القائلين بالمفهوم لا يقولون باستلزام رفع المقدم رفع التالي إنما يقولون بدلالة التركيب على الانتفاء عند الانتفاء، كما أنه يدل على تعليق الوجود بالوجود وهذا بعينه مثله مثل لو فإنه يدل على انتفاء الجزاء لانتفاء الشرط، ولك أن تقرر الاستدلال هكذا: لو كان المفهوم مدلول الكلام لاستلزم رفع المقدم رفع التالي لغة ولما صح استعمال أدوات الشرط فيما إذا كان المقدم أخص لغة، وهذا كله باطل لا ينبغي لأحد التزامه فافهم، ولا استحالة في لو فإنه خصوصاً لا يستعمل لغة إلا فيما يكونان متساويين مستحيلين عرفاً أو عقلاً ولا استحالة فيه، وأما لو كان المفهوم حقاً فيلزم عدم استعمال أدوات الشرط كلها في الأخص والأعم أصلاً، وشناعته بينة فافهم. مثبتو مفهوم الشرط قالوا: أولاً يلزم من انتفاء الشرط انتفاء المشروط) وهو المفهوم (ولا يخفى أنه اشتباه من اشتراك الاسم إذ الكلام في الشرط النحوي ولا يلزم انتفائه انتفاء الجزاء، والمستدل أخذ الشرط العقلي أو الشرعي الذي يتوقف عليه المشروط من على أنه ربما يكون) الشرط (شرطاً لإيقاع الحكم من المتكلم (لا) لثبوته) في الواقع، فلا يلزم انتفائه إلا انتفاء الإيقاع، وهو المسكوت بعينه، فإن قلت إذا انتفى الإيقاع الإنشائي انتفى الحكم إذ هو المثبت لا غيره، قلت: هذا بالحقيقة يرجع إلى نفي المفهوم، والرجوع إلى التمسك بالأصل، فإن لم يكن هناك إنشاء آخر مثبت للحكم ينتفي بانتفاء العلة، وهذا ليس من المفهوم في شيء، وإن كان إنشاء آخر يثبت الحكم به لا بهذا الإنشاء فافهم. ولما كان هذا اشتباهاً فعدلوا منه إلى أن استعمال "أن" في السببية أي سببية الأول للثاني غالباً والأصل عدم الأسباب فينتفي المسبب بانتفائه غالباً وهو المفهوم. قلنا: لا نسلم استعماله للسببية غالباً، فإنه كثيراً ما يستعمل في المتلازمين والمتضايفين مع أنه لا سببية للأول، ولو سلم استعماله في السببية غالباً فهذا ليس باللفظ دلالة حتى يكون النفي حكماً شرعياً.
And among them is the concept of condition: that the judgment is negated when the condition is negated, and it is like the concept of attribute. That is, the concept of condition is like the concept of attribute. It is said that it is stronger than it. All those who affirm the concept of attribute affirm it, and some of those who do not affirm it, like the Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi from our scholars, affirm it. For us, what has been established rationally and customarily is that the removal of the antecedent does not entail the removal of the consequent, as in His statement (Quran 24:33). And it is objected against him that those who affirm the concept do not say that the removal of the antecedent entails the removal of the consequent; rather, they say that the composition indicates negation upon negation, just as it indicates the attachment of existence to existence. This is exactly like 'law' (if), for it indicates the negation of the consequence due to the negation of the condition. You may state the inference thus: if the concept were the meaning of the speech, then the removal of the antecedent would necessitate the removal of the consequent linguistically, and it would not be correct to use conditional particles when the antecedent is more specific linguistically. All of this is false and no one should adhere to it. Understand. And there is no impossibility in 'law', for it is specifically used linguistically only when [the two parts] are equally impossible customarily or rationally, and there is no impossibility in it. As for if the concept were true, it would necessitate that conditional particles are not used at all in the specific and general, and its ugliness is clear. Understand. The affirmers of the concept of condition said: first, the negation of the condition necessitates the negation of the conditioned, which is the concept. It is not hidden that this is a confusion due to homonymy, for the discussion is about a grammatical condition, and its negation does not necessitate the negation of the consequence. The arguer took the rational or legal condition upon which the conditioned depends, and that perhaps the condition is a condition for the enactment of the judgment by the speaker, not for its existence in reality. So its negation only necessitates the negation of the enactment, which is exactly what is silent. If you say: if the enacting/performative is negated, the judgment is negated, for it is the affirmant and nothing else, I say: this actually reduces to the denial of the concept, and a return to adherence to the original [principle of non-necessity]. If there is no other enactment affirming the judgment, it is negated due to the negation of the cause, and this is not part of the concept at all. And if there is another enactment affirming the judgment through it, not through this enactment, then understand. Since this was a confusion, they turned from it to [arguing] that the use of 'an' (that) in causation, i.e. the causality of the first for the second, is predominant, and the original is the absence of causes, so the caused ceases with its negation predominantly, and that is the concept. We say: we do not accept that it is predominantly used for causation, for it is often used for concomitants and correlatives despite there being no causality of the first. And if it is conceded that it is used for causation predominantly, this is not a linguistic indication such that the negation is a legal ruling.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the validity of mafhum al-shart (the concept of condition). The Hanafi position, which the author defends, rejects mafhum al-shart as a valid legal proof. The passage begins by defining mafhum al-shart as the negation of the ruling when the condition is negated, likening it to mafhum al-sifa (concept of attribute). Some scholars, including Imam al-Karkhi from the Hanafi school, affirm mafhum al-shart and consider it stronger than mafhum al-sifa. The Hanafi proof against mafhum al-shart is rational and customary: the removal of the antecedent (muqaddam) does not entail the removal of the consequent (tali). They cite the Quranic verse (24:33) which prohibits coercion of slave girls to fornication if they desire chastity. The verse implies that if they do not desire chastity, coercion is not prohibited? Actually, according to those who reject mafhum al-shart, the verse does not negate the prohibition when the condition (desire for chastity) is absent; the prohibition might still apply for other reasons. The opponents counter that they do not claim entailment (istilzam) but rather that the linguistic structure indicates negation upon negation. They compare it to the particle 'law' (if) which indicates that the consequence is negated when the condition is negated. The Hanafi response is that if mafhum were the actual meaning, conditional particles would only be used when the antecedent and consequent are coextensive, but in fact they are used when the antecedent is more specific (akhass) or more general (a'amm), which would be impossible. Thus the Hanafis argue that mafhum al-shart is not a valid linguistic indication. The proponents then shift to a causal argument: the particle 'an' (that) is predominantly used for causation, and since causes are absent by default, the effect is negated when the cause is absent. The Hanafis respond that causation is not predominant; the particle is also used for concomitance (talazum) and correlation (tada'uf) without causality. And even if it were causal, that would not be a linguistic indication for a legal ruling. The passage thus firmly establishes the Hanafi rejection of mafhum al-shart.

Key Terms
مفهوم الشرط (mafhum al-shart): The concept of condition: the understanding that when a condition is negated, the conditioned (ruling) is also negated.
رفع المقدم (raf' al-muqaddam): The removal or negation of the antecedent (the condition in a conditional statement).
رفع التالي (raf' al-tali): The removal or negation of the consequent (the apodosis or result).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best represents the Hanafi position on mafhum al-shart (concept of condition)?
A) It is a valid proof for deriving legal rulings.
B) It is valid only in cases of clear causation.
C) It is not a valid proof; the negation of a condition does not necessitate negation of the ruling.
D) It is stronger than mafhum al-sifa (concept of attribute).

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-shart is rejected in Hanafi usul; negation of a condition does not necessitate negation of the ruling.

Mafhum al-Shart: Definition and Hanafi Rejection
Definition and Hanafi rejection of conditional concept

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mafhum al-shart and explain the rational proof against its validity as a linguistic implication.

Core Idea
Negating the condition does not linguistically negate the ruling.

This lesson examines the concept of mafhum al-shart, a central topic in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school argues that the absence of a condition does not automatically imply the absence of the ruling, using rational and linguistic reasoning. We will analyze the definition, the proof from the Quran, the objection from proponents, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and definition
Mafhum al-shart is defined as the absence of the ruling when the condition is absent. Understand its relationship to mafhum al-sifah.
The passage compares it to mafhum al-sifah and notes that some consider it stronger.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is both rational and conventional: raising the antecedent does not entail raising the consequent. This is supported by the Quranic verse from Surah al-Nur (24:33).
The verse prohibits compulsion 'if they desire chastity' — it does not imply permission when they do not.
3
Analyze the objection
Proponents (like al-Karkhi) argue that the construction itself indicates negation upon negation, similar to the particle 'law'.
They claim the implication is linguistic, not logical.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
If the implication were linguistic, conditional particles could not be used when the antecedent is more specific than the consequent, but they are used. This refutes the claimed linguistic necessity.
The particle 'law' is a special case used only when antecedent and consequent are equal.
5
Apply to a case
Consider the verse: without mafhum al-shart, we do not infer permissibility from the absence of the condition. The ruling remains on its original basis (e.g., prohibition of compulsion).
The practical difference (thamarah) is clear: proponents would permit compulsion if the slave-girls do not desire chastity; Hanafis do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Among them is the concept of condition: it is the absence of the ruling upon the absence of the condition, and it is like the concept of attribute. That is, the concept of condition is like the concept of attribute. And it is said that it is stronger than it. Those who affirm the concept of attribute all affirm it, and some who do not affirm it also affirm it, such as the Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi from our scholars. For us, it has been established both rationally and conventionally that raising the antecedent does not indicate raising the consequent, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'And do not compel your slave girls to prostitution, if they desire chastity' [al-Nur 24:33]. And it was objected that those who affirm the concept do not claim that raising the antecedent entails raising the consequent; rather, they claim that the construction indicates the negation upon negation, just as it indicates the linking of existence with existence. This is exactly like 'law' (if) which indicates the negation of the consequence due to the negation of the condition. And you can present the proof as follows: if the concept were the implication of the speech, it would require that raising the antecedent entails raising the consequent linguistically, and it would not be valid to use conditional particles when the antecedent is more specific linguistically. All of this is false and should not be accepted by anyone. Understand. And there is no impossibility in 'law' because it is specifically not used linguistically except in cases where the two are equal, both conventionally and rationally impossible, and there is no impossibility in it. And if the concept were true, it would necessitate the non-use of all conditional particles in the specific and the general entirely, and its offensiveness is apparent. Understand.

Commentary
This passage defines 'mafhum al-shart' (concept of condition) and presents the Hanafi position that it is not a valid linguistic implication. The author explains that removing the antecedent does not entail removing the consequent, citing the Quranic verse about not forcing slave-girls into prostitution if they desire chastity. The objection by proponents of the concept is addressed: they claim that the construction itself indicates the absence of the verdict when the condition is absent. The Hanafi response is that if that were linguistically true, conditional particles could not be used when the antecedent is more specific, which is false. Therefore, the concept is not a valid proof.

Key Terms
مفهوم الشرط (mafhum al-shart): The inferred ruling that when the condition is absent, the ruling is absent.
مفهوم الصفة (mafhum al-sifah): The inferred ruling that when an attribute is absent, the ruling attached to it is absent.
رفع المقدم (raf' al-muqaddam): Negation or removal of the antecedent (the condition) in a conditional statement.
رفع التالي (raf' al-tali): Negation or removal of the consequent (the ruling) in a conditional statement.

D) Only in the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-shart is not a valid proof (dalil) in Hanafi usul; the absence of a condition does not linguistically necessitate the absence of the ruling.
