The Hanafi Position on Ta'liq: Condition Blocks the Cause
States the Hanafi position on whether a condition prevents the cause from being effective or the ruling from being established.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ta'liq and explain how it differs from the Shafi'i position, and identify the consequence for mafhum al-shart.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, a condition prevents the cause from being a cause; for Shafi'is, it only blocks the ruling.

This lesson introduces a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute: what exactly does a condition (shart) do when it suspends a ruling? Does it block the cause (sabab) from operating, or does it merely prevent the ruling from appearing in that specific case? The answer affects how we understand conditional statements and the validity of mafhum al-shart. We will examine the Hanafi view and its contrast with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dispute
Identify the two positions: Hanafis say the condition prevents the cause from being a cause; Shafi'is say it prevents the ruling from being established.
2
Locate the effect
For Hanafis, when the condition is absent, the cause is not effective, so no ruling arises. For Shafi'is, the cause remains a cause but the ruling is absent due to the missing condition.
3
Connect to mafhum al-shart
This difference grounds the disagreement on the concept of condition (mafhum al-shart): Hanafis reject it because absence of ruling is due to negation of cause, not linguistic implication; Shafi'is accept it because absence of condition directly implies absence of ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة التعليق هل يمنع السبب عن السببية أو الحكم عن الثبوت (فقط) لا السبب عن الانعقاد اختار الحنفية الأول والشافعية (الثاني) والقاضي الإمام أبو زيد والإمام فخر الإسلام بنيا عليه مسألة مفهوم الشرط، وقرر صاحب الكشف وغيره وجه الابتناء بأنه لما مال الشافعية إلى أن الجزاء سبب للحكم وموجب له والشرط يمنع ثبوت الحكم عند عدمه، فعدم الحكم لعدم الشرط عنده وعندنا لما منعه عن السببية وإيجاب الحكم عند عدمه فعدم الحكم لانتفاء السبب
Issue: Does the conditional suspension (ta'liq) prevent the cause from being a cause, or only prevent the ruling from being established (but not the cause from being effective)? The Hanafis chose the first, and the Shafi'is the second. And the chief judge Abu Zaid and the chief of Islam Fakhr al-Islam based upon it the issue of the concept of condition. And the author of al-Kashf and others formulated the basis as follows: since the Shafi'is inclined to the view that the consequence (jazaa) is a cause for the ruling and gives it effect, and the condition prevents the establishment of the ruling in its absence, so the absence of the ruling in their view is due to the absence of the condition. And in our view, because it (the condition) prevents the cause from being a cause and from giving the ruling in its absence, so the absence of the ruling is due to the negation of the cause.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This brief passage presents a key difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i usul regarding the role of a condition. According to Hanafis, a condition blocks the cause (sabab) from being effective, meaning that when the condition is absent, the cause does not operate to produce the ruling. For Shafi'is, the condition only prevents the ruling from being established for that particular case, but the cause itself remains a cause in principle. This difference underlies their respective positions on mafhum al-shart. For Shafi'is, when the condition is absent, the ruling is absent because the condition is missing; for Hanafis, the ruling is absent because the cause is not operative without the condition. The passage also notes that earlier Hanafi scholars like al-Qadi Abu Zaid and Fakhr al-Islam built their position on mafhum al-shart based on this principle.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): The suspension of a ruling on a condition.
سبب (sabab): The cause that normally produces a legal ruling.
حكم (hukm): The legal ruling that is conditionally suspended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, what does a condition prevent when it is absent in a conditional statement?
A) The ruling from being established.
B) The cause from being a cause (i.e., from giving the ruling).
C) The text from being applicable.
D) The condition itself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a condition in a conditional legal statement blocks the cause from being effective, not merely the ruling, which explains their rejection of the concept of condition (mafhum al-shart).

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Conditional Sentences: Does Mafhum al-Shart Hold?
Analyzing Hanafi vs Shafi'i on conditional clauses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on conditional sentences and apply the principle that the apodosis alone conveys no ruling to derive the Hanafi view on mafhum al-shart.

Core Idea
The apodosis alone gives no ruling; the entire conditional conveys a suspensive ruling.

This passage addresses a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: do conditional clauses imply that the consequence is negated when the condition is absent? The Hanafi school, following logicians, argues that the apodosis alone does not indicate any ruling; rather, the composite of condition and apodosis yields a suspensive ruling. The Shafi'i school, following grammarians, holds that the apodosis conveys a general ruling that is specified by the condition. The differences have practical implications for interpreting legal texts and for the validity of mafhum al-shart as a proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on the conditional sentence
State what each school claims about the apodosis (الجزاء) and the condition. The Hanafi view: the apodosis alone conveys no ruling; the conditional as a whole conveys a suspensive ruling (حكم تعليقي). The Shafi'i view: the apodosis conveys a general ruling, and the condition specifies it.
This is the core of the dispute.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof from logic
Understand why Abu Hanifa holds that the composite (condition + apodosis) conveys a suspensive ruling, not the apodosis alone. The key phrase: 'فالجزاء عنده لا يدل على حكم أصلاً، وإنما المفيد المجموع الحكم المقيد' (the apodosis indicates no ruling at all; rather the composite conveys the qualified ruling). This is based on the nature of conditional propositions in logic.
The Hanafi view avoids requiring actuality of the apodosis.
3
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Apply the two views to a concrete scenario: a husband says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' Under the Shafi'i view, the apodosis gives a ruling (divorce occurs upon entry) and by mafhum al-shart, if entry never occurs, the ruling is negated (no divorce). Under the Hanafi view, the composite gives a suspensive ruling: divorce is suspended upon entry; if entry never occurs, the original state (marriage) continues unchanged, but mafhum al-shart does not apply because the apodosis alone does not give a ruling.
The practical difference is whether absence of condition implies negation of the consequence.
4
Evaluate the three critiques of the Shafi'i position
The author presents three critiques. First: If the apodosis conveyed a ruling that requires actuality, it would be false because the apodosis may be impossible while the conditional is valid. Second: Even if the apodosis conveys a qualified ruling (by condition), the qualification prevents the ruling from applying universally, so negation upon absence does not follow. Third: Even if we accept both views, the dispute remains: does the composite (by explicit wording) indicate negation upon absence? The Hanafi view says no.
These critiques reinforce the Hanafi stance that mafhum al-shart is not a valid proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية (و) مال (أبو حنيفة إلى الثاني) فهو مع الشرط أفاد حكماً تعليقياً عنده فلم يوجد الحكم منه بوقوع الجزاء، بل إنما يتحقق عند وجود الشرط، إذ قد أفاد حكماً تعليقياً، فبقي فيما وراء المعلق عليه على ما كان عليه في الأصل، فههنا :مطلبان الأول تفرع مفهوم الشرط على هذا الخلاف، وتقريره أن الشافعي لما مال إلى مذهب أهل العربية كان الجزاء عنده مفيداً للحكم على والشرط خصصه، فالنفي مضاف إليه، والإمام أبو حنيفة لما مال إلى قول أهل الميزان فالجزاء عنده لا يدل على حكم أصلاً، وإنما المفيد المجموع الحكم المقيد، فلا يدل العدم عند العدم بل العدم يبقى أصلاً كما كان هذا حاصل كلامه وفيه بحث، أما أولاً : فلأنه إن أراد بإفادة الجزاء الحكم حال الشرط أنه مفيد لثبوت الحكم في الواقع، لكن على تقدير وجود الشرط فيه فيلزم لصدقه تحقق الجزاء البتة والشرط أيضاً فهذا فاسد، فإن الجزاء ربما يكون مستحيلاً مع كون الشرطية مستعملة عرفاً ولغة فبناء الكلام على هذا الباطل لا يليق، وكيف يقول أمثال هذا الإمام الهمام ذو اليد الطولى في العلوم وإن أراد بها إفادة كون حكم الجزاء ثابتاً على تقدير وجود الشرط على سبيل القضية التقديرية ولا يستلزم صدقها صدق الجزاء في الواقع، بل على تقدير الشرط لا غير، فهذا مساوق للشرطية فما يلزم من كون الحكم في الجزاء إلا ما يلزم من كون الحكم بينهما للتلازم فافهم وأما ثانياً، فلأنا سلمنا ذلك ولا نسلم أن الجزاء على هذا التقدير يستدعي الحكم على جميع التقادير والشرط خصصه، بل الجزاء حينئذ مقيد بالحال أو الظرف وإذا كان في الكلام قيد يبقى موقوفاً عليه ويستفاد من المجموع حكم مقيد، فلا يلزم منه العدم عند العدم بل يبقى على ما كان لو بنى على أنه قائل بكون الشرط مخصصاً للجزاء، وهو إنما يكون لو كان الجزاء مقيداً لعموم التقادير كما قدمنا لكان له وجه، لكن لا يفي لإثباته كون الجزاء خبراً والشرط بمنزلة الحل والظرف، وأما ثالثاً : فلأنا سلمنا ذلك، لكن النزاع باق لا ينفع الحنفية الذهاب إلى قول أهل المنطق أيضاً لأنه مسلم أن المجموع مفيد لحكم تعليقي بالمنطوق وهل يدل في المسكوت انتفاء الجزاء بعدم الشرط أم لا، ولا يلزم تعين أحدهما فالنزاع باق كما كان فافهم وإذا تأملت علمت أن هذا وارد على ما قررنا من البناء فتدبر .
The third article on linguistic principles. (And) Abu Hanifa inclined to the second (view): for him, the conditional together with the protasis yields a suspensive ruling, so the ruling is not actualized by the apodosis alone; rather it is realized only when the condition exists, since it has yielded a suspensive ruling, thus what lies beyond the condition remains as it was originally. Here there are two demands: first, the branching of the concept of condition on this dispute. Its explanation: al-Shafi'i, when he inclined to the school of the Arab grammarians, considered the apodosis to convey the ruling, and the condition specifies it, so negation is attributed to it. Imam Abu Hanifa, when he inclined to the view of the logicians, held that the apodosis does not indicate any ruling at all; rather the composite (i.e., the conditional sentence) conveys the qualified ruling, so non-existence upon non-existence does not follow; rather non-existence remains as it was originally. This is the summary of his words, and there is discussion. First: if by 'the apodosis conveying the ruling' he means that it conveys the affirmation of the ruling in reality, but upon the assumption of the existence of the condition within it, then its truth would necessitate the actual occurrence of the apodosis and also the condition—this is invalid, for the apodosis may be impossible while the conditional is used customarily and linguistically; building speech on this falsehood is unbefitting. If he means that it conveys the affirmation of the ruling of the apodosis upon the assumption of the existence of the condition in the manner of a hypothetical proposition, and its truth does not entail the truth of the apodosis in reality, but only upon the assumption of the condition, then this is equivalent to the conditional; so what follows from the ruling being in the apodosis is nothing but what follows from the ruling being between them due to entailment—understand. Second: even if we accept that, we do not accept that the apodosis upon this assumption demands the ruling for all assumptions while the condition specifies it; rather the apodosis then is qualified by a state or circumstance, and if there is a qualification in the speech, it remains pending on it, and from the composite a qualified ruling is derived; so non-existence upon non-existence does not follow, but rather remains as it was. If one builds on the view that the condition is a specifier of the apodosis, that would only be if the apodosis were qualified for a general set of assumptions as we mentioned, then it would have a basis, but it does not suffice to prove it that the apodosis is a predicate and the condition is like a state or circumstance. Third: even if we accept that, the dispute remains; it does not benefit the Hanafis to adopt the view of the logicians as well, because it is accepted that the composite conveys a suspensive ruling by the explicit wording, but does it indicate in the silent (part) the negation of the apodosis upon the absence of the condition or not? Neither one is necessarily determined; the dispute remains as it was—understand. And if you reflect, you will know that this applies to what we established from the construction—ponder.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the interpretation of conditional sentences (الجملة الشرطية) and their legal implications. The issue is: does a conditional clause (e.g., 'If you enter, you are divorced') imply that the consequence (divorce) is negated when the condition is absent? Al-Shafi'i, following the Arab grammarians, holds that the apodosis (الجزاء) itself conveys a general ruling, and the condition specifies it; thus when the condition is absent, the ruling is negated (مفهوم الشرط). Abu Hanifa, following the logicians (أهل الميزان), holds that the entire conditional sentence conveys a suspensive ruling (حكم تعليقي) – a linkage between condition and consequence – but the apodosis alone does not convey any ruling. Therefore, the absence of the condition does not necessarily negate the consequence; the original state (e.g., marriage) remains as is. The author then presents three critiques of the Shafi'i position and defends the Hanafi view. The passage also branches into two sub-issues: (1) the concept of condition (مفهوم الشرط) and (2) causality (السببية) – whether the conditional sentence itself is a cause for the consequence. The author argues that the Hanafi view correctly denies causality from the conditional sentence alone.

Key Terms
مفهوم الشرط (mafhūm al-sharṭ): The understood meaning that when the condition is absent, the consequence is negated.
السببية (al-sababiyya): Causality: whether the conditional sentence itself is a cause for the occurrence of the consequence.
حكم تعليقي (ḥukm taʿlīqī): A suspensive ruling that is contingent upon a condition; the ruling is not actual until the condition occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view on conditional sentences in usul al-fiqh, what does the apodosis (الجزاء) alone convey?
A) A general ruling that is specified by the condition.
B) A suspensive ruling that is actualized when the condition occurs.
C) No ruling at all; the entire conditional conveys a qualified ruling.
D) A hypothetical ruling that is always actualized.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conditional sentences do not imply negation of the consequence when the condition is absent; they convey a suspensive ruling from the composite, not from the apodosis alone.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Mafhum al-Ghayah: The Hanafi Position on Limits in Legal Texts
Definition and dispute over whether a limit implies negation beyond it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi view on mafhum al-ghayah from the Shafi'i/Mu'tazila view, and apply the Hanafi critique to a given textual example.

Core Idea
A limit (ghayah) does not automatically negate the ruling beyond it; it may merely indicate the speaker's scope.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut introduces the concept of mafhum al-ghayah (concept of the limit) and the central dispute between the Hanafi school and those who affirm it as a binding linguistic principle. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting Quranic and hadith texts that contain explicit limits, such as 'until night' in the fasting verse. The Hanafis argue that the limit only marks the end of the speaker's statement, not necessarily the end of the actual ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept being defined
What is mafhum al-ghayah? It is the claim that when a legal text mentions a limit (e.g., 'until'), the ruling is negated after that limit. This is affirmed by some Shafi'is and Mu'tazila.
The well-known definition is that it negates the ruling after the limit.
2
Understand the affirmative position and its proof
Those who affirm mafhum al-ghayah argue: if the limit did not negate the ruling beyond, it would not be a limit, because the ruling would apply beyond it.
Their proof: 'If it were not a concept, the limit would not be a limit.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi objections
The passage presents three Hanafi counter-arguments: (1) The dispute might be about the limit itself, not after; (2) The speaker's statement ending at the limit only shows non-reference, not actual negation; (3) Even if we grant negation, it could be mere indication (ishara), not a linguistic concept.
The third objection is attributed to Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma.
4
Distinguish the dispute: limit itself vs. after the limit
Note that some say the disagreement is only about whether the limit itself is included in the ruling, not about what follows. This nuance reduces the scope of the dispute.
The Hanafis may accept negation for the limit itself but not for after.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Apply the Hanafi view to Quran 2:187 'then complete the fast until night': the limit does not automatically prohibit fasting after night; the end of fasting is known from other evidence, not from the limit alone.
The Shafi'i would say the limit itself negates the obligation after night.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها مفهوم الغاية، قال به (القاضي من الشافعية وعبد الجبار) من المعتزلة (أيضاً) كما قال به كل من يقول بمفهوم الصفة والشرط والمشهور) في تفسير مفهوم الغاية (أنه نفي الحكم فيما بعد الغاية، فقالوا في الاستدلال (لو لم يكن مفهوم الغاية مفهوماً (لم تكن الغاية غاية، إذ لو تناول الحكم لما بعدها لم يكن الحكم منتهياً إليها وقيل : النزاع في نفس الغاية) فالقائل بمفهومها يقول بانتفاء الحكم فيها ومن لا فلا (لا) فيما بعدها وعلى هذا الملازمة ممنوعة) كيف وقد مر الخلاف في أنّ الغاية هل تدخل في حكم المغيا؟ (وأيضاً) غاية ما لزم منه انتهاء حكم المتكلم فينقطع إليه الحكم النفسي وانقطاع الحكم النفسي بهذا الكلام مسلم، لكن لا ينفعكم فإنه إنما يستلزم عدم التعرض فيها وفيما بعدها، ولا يلزم منه انقطاع الحكم في الواقع (وأيضاً) نسلم إنتفاء الحكم فيها وفيما بعدها، لكن لا يلزم المفهومية، لجواز أن يكون هذا النفي إشارة، كما هو قول مشايخنا الكرام من الإمام فخر الإسلام وشمس
And among them is the concept of the limit (ghayah). It is affirmed by (al-Qadi from the Shafi'is and Abdul Jabbar) from the Mu'tazila (also), as affirmed by everyone who affirms the concept of attribute and condition. And the well-known (view) in the interpretation of the concept of ghayah is that it is the negation of the ruling after the limit. They said in argument: If the concept of the limit were not a concept, then the limit would not be a limit, because if the ruling applied to what comes after it, the ruling would not terminate at it. And it is said: The dispute is about the limit itself: the one who affirms its concept says the ruling is negated within it, and the one who does not says the opposite, not (about) what comes after it. Based on this, the entailment is denied; how, when the dispute about whether the limit is included in the ruling of the limited (maghya) has already passed? (Also) the utmost that follows from it is the termination of the speaker's ruling, and the psychological ruling is cut off at it; the interruption of the psychological ruling by this speech is granted, but it does not benefit you, for it only implies non-reference to it and what comes after it, and it does not necessitate the interruption of the actual ruling. (Also) we grant the negation of the ruling in it and after it, but it does not necessitate the conceptuality, because it is possible that this negation is an indication, as is the statement of our noble scholars from (Imam Fakhr al-Islam and Shams)...
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of ghayah (limit) in usul al-fiqh, focusing on whether the mention of a limit in a legal text (e.g., 'until night' in fasting) carries the concept (mafhum) that the ruling is negated beyond that limit. The author first states that this concept is affirmed by some Shafi'is and Mu'tazila, and by those who affirm concepts of attribute and condition. The well-known definition is that it negates the ruling after the limit. Their proof: if it were not a concept, the limit would not be a limit. The passage then presents objections from the Hanafi perspective: (1) The dispute might be about the limit itself, not after; (2) Even if the speaker's statement ends at the limit, this only indicates non-reference, not actual negation of the ruling in reality; (3) Even if we grant negation, it does not prove a linguistic concept, because the negation might be merely an indication (ishara) and not a necessary implication. The Hanafis thus reject the concept of ghayah as a binding linguistic principle.

Key Terms
مفهوم الغاية (mafhum al-ghayah): The concept that the ruling of a text is limited to what is mentioned before the limit and does not apply after it.
الغاية (al-ghayah): A limit or end point mentioned in a legal text, such as 'until' (ila, hatta, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the status of the concept of ghayah (mafhum al-ghayah)?
A) It is a decisive proof (qat'i) that negates the ruling beyond the limit.
B) It is a valid concept but only in the Quran.
C) It is not a necessary linguistic concept; the negation may be merely an indication.
D) It is accepted if the limit is explicit and clear.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not recognize mafhum al-ghayah as a binding principle; a limit indicates the scope of the speech but does not automatically negate the ruling beyond.

Mafhum al-Adad (Concept of Number) and the Hanafi Dispute
Explains the concept of number with its proof and the disagreement among Hanafis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on mafhum al-adad and apply the distinction between dalalat al-nass and qiyas to evaluate the ruling on killing harmful beasts.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-adad is contested among Hanafis: some reject it, some accept it, affecting rulings by analogy.

The concept of number (mafhum al-adad) is a debated tool in Hanafi usul. When a ruling specifies a number, does it linguistically imply that the ruling applies only to that number? This lesson unpacks the disagreement among Hanafi scholars, using the Quranic verse on eighty lashes and the hadith of five pests as key proof texts. You will explore both sides and see how this dispute plays out in rulings on killing harmful animals during ihram.

Guided Path
1
Define mafhum al-adad
State the definition: the implication that a ruling tied to a specific number does not apply beyond that number.
Example: 'eighty lashes' implies no more than eighty.
2
Identify the primary proof
Locate the Quranic verse (Surah An-Nur:4) in the passage and note how it is used as an example of mafhum al-adad.
The verse specifies eighty lashes for false accusation.
3
Map the Hanafi internal dispute
List the two positions: those who reject mafhum al-adad (Fakhr al-Islam, Shams al-A'immah) and those who accept it (al-Tahawi, Abu Bakr al-Razi).
Note that the rejection is based on lack of evidence for increase, not on linguistic denial.
4
Analyze the supporting arguments
Examine the hadith of five pests and the addition of the wolf. Understand how it supports both sides, depending on whether the wolf is included in 'vicious dog'.
The passage states that the acceptance view relies on the wolf not being included, making the addition a qiyas.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: for those who accept mafhum al-adad, killing other harmful beasts is not permitted by analogy; for those who reject it, it is permitted by qiyas.
The response to al-Shafi'i hinges on whether the permissibility is from dalalat al-nass or qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها مفهوم العدد وهو نفي الحكم الثابت بعدد معين عما زاد عليه كقوله تعالى : وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَتِ ثُمَّ لَوْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَنِينَ جَلْدَةً ﴾ [النور: ٤] فيفهم منه عدم جلد ما زاد على ثمانين واختلف الحنفية فيه فمنهم منكر له كالإمام فخر الإسلام وشمس وغيرهما كالبيضاوي وإمام الحرمين والقاضي أبي بكر كلهم من الشافعية، ونفي الزيادة على ثمانين بعدم الدليل، والأصل عدم إيجاع المسلم من غير حق، كما يشهد به قوله عليه وعلى آله الصلاة والسلام المسلم من سلم المسلمون من لسانه ويده ويؤيده الزيادة على الخمس الفواسق المذكورة في حديث: خمس من الدواب ليس على المحرم في قتلهن جناح العقرب والفأرة والكلب العقور والغراب والحدأة ، رواه الشيخان كالذئب فعلم أن حكم ما زاد مثله لا خلافه، وهذا التأييد إنما يتم لو لم يكن الذئب داخلاً في الكلب العقور وقيل: المراد بالكلب العقور الذئب وأما جواز قتل الكلب العقور فلأنه ليس من الصيد ومنهم قائل كالطحاوي، وقال الشيخ أبو بكر الرازي: قد كنت أسمع كثيراً من شيوخنا يقولون في المخصوص بالعدد يدل على أن ما عداه حكمه بخلافه، كذا في التقرير كذا في الحاشية ويؤيده، ما في الهداية رداً على الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى في إباحة قتل الأسد وغيره من السباع المؤذية القياس على الفواسق ممتنع ، لما فيه من إبطال العدد هذا وإنما يتم التأييد لو لم يكن إلزاماً وقيل : الردّ غير تام لأنه ثابت بدلالة النص دون القياس والثابت بالدلالة ليس زيادة، وأيضاً لو كان بالقياس فهو قاض على المفهوم فتدبر.
And among them is the concept of number, which is the negation of the ruling established by a specific number to what exceeds it, as in His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses – lash them eighty lashes' [An-Nur:4]. So it is understood from it the non-flogging for more than eighty. The Hanafis differed concerning it: among them is one who rejects it, like Imam Fakhr al-Islam and Shams and others, and like al-Baydawi, Imam al-Haramayn, and Qadi Abu Bakr – all of them Shafi'is. He denies the increase beyond eighty due to lack of evidence, and the principle is the non-infliction of harm upon a Muslim without right, as is witnessed by his statement, peace be upon him and his family: 'The Muslim is the one from whose tongue and hand the Muslims are safe.' And it is supported by the increase beyond the five pests mentioned in the hadith: 'Five types of creatures for which there is no sin upon the Muhrim in killing them: the scorpion, the mouse, the vicious dog, the crow, and the kite' – narrated by the two Shaykhs – like the wolf. Thus it is known that the ruling of what is similar to it is like it, not different. This support is only valid if the wolf is not included in the vicious dog, and it is said: what is meant by the vicious dog is the wolf. As for the permissibility of killing the vicious dog, it is because it is not game. And among them is one who asserts it, like al-Tahawi. And Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Razi said: I used to hear many of our teachers say concerning what is specified by number that it indicates that the ruling of other than it is contrary to it, as in al-Taqrir, as in al-Hashiyah. And it is supported by what is in al-Hidayah as a response to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding the permissibility of killing the lion and other harmful beasts: analogy to the five pests is impermissible because it nullifies the number. This support is only valid if it is not an entailing argument. And it is said: the response is incomplete because it is established by the indication of the text (dalalat al-nass) not by analogy, and what is established by indication is not an increase. Also, if it were by analogy, it would override the concept (mafhum), so reflect.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of number (mafhum al-adad) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The concept means that when a specific number is mentioned in a ruling, it implies that the ruling does not apply to anything beyond that number. The example is the Quranic verse on flogging for false accusation: eighty lashes, implying no more than eighty. The author then notes a dispute among Hanafis: some, like Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, reject this concept, arguing that the negation of increase is based on lack of evidence rather than linguistic implication. They cite the hadith about five pests allowed to be killed in ihram; when the wolf was added by scholars, they saw it as an analogy not contradicting the concept. Others, like al-Tahawi and Abu Bakr al-Razi, accept the concept, citing that the indication of a specific number shows the opposite ruling for other numbers. The text then discusses a response to al-Shafi'i regarding killing harmful beasts: analogy to the five pests is rejected because it would nullify the number. The discussion highlights the tension between textual implication (mafhum) and analogical reasoning (qiyas), concluding that if a ruling is established by dalalat al-nass (textual indication), it is like a textual ruling and not subject to qiyas overriding it.

Key Terms
مفهوم العدد (mafhum al-‘adad): The linguistic implication that a specific number in a ruling negates that ruling for anything beyond that number.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): Textual indication: a ruling derived directly from the wording of the text without reliance on analogy or independent reasoning.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main argument used by the Hanafis who reject mafhum al-adad about the eighty lashes verse?
A) The verse explicitly states the number, so no inference is needed.
B) The increase beyond eighty is negated by lack of evidence, not by linguistic implication.
C) The hadith of the five pests proves that numbers can be exceeded by analogy.
D) The verse is abrogated and no longer applicable.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-adad is a contested concept in Hanafi usul; its acceptance or rejection leads to different rulings on whether a specified number restricts the application of a ruling.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Mafhum al-Laqab: Definition and Scholarly Positions
Defines mafhum al-laqub and lists supporters and opponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mafhum al-laqub and identify which schools accept or reject it.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-laqub: the concept that a title exclusively carries the ruling — rejected by Hanafis.

In usul al-fiqh, the concept of title (mafhum al-laqub) refers to the implication that a ruling applies only to the named entity, and the opposite applies to everything else. This principle is not universally accepted. In this lesson, we will define it and map the scholarly positions.

Guided Path
1
Define Mafhum al-Laqab
Start with the definition from the passage: it is the establishment of a ruling contrary to the articulated ruling for what is beyond the title. Understand that it applies to proper names and generic nouns.
Example: 'Zayd is standing' would imply that no one else is standing.
2
Identify the Schools that Accept It
According to the passage, some Hanbalis, a few Shafi'is (called al-diqaq), and some Malikis accept it.
The term 'al-diqaq' refers to the subtle-minded among the Shafi'is.
3
Identify the Schools that Reject It
The majority of Hanafis and others reject it. This is the dominant Hanafi position.
The rejection is based on conditions and consequences.
4
Understand the Underlying Condition
The passage mentions that a valid concept requires the absence of benefit (i.e., the concept should not add new information). In mafhum al-laqub, there is benefit in specifying the subject, so it fails this condition.
This condition is similarly applied to concepts of attribute and condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها مفهوم اللقب وهو ثبوت الحكم المخالف للمنطوق فيما وراء اللقب والمراد ما يعم اسم الجنس قال به بعض الحنابلة والدقاق من الشافعية والمنداد من المالكية والجمهور من الحنفية وغيرهم منكرون إياه للجمهور أولاً أنه طريق متعين لتعبير المحكوم عليه بالمنطوق، لأنه لولاه لاختل المنطوق، وهو من أعظم الفوائد ولازم في كل كلام، ومن شرط المفهوم انتفاء الفوائد، وهذا جار بعينه في الصفة والشرط كما عرفت و للجمهور، ثانياً لزوم كفر من قال محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم على تقدير ثبوت مفهوم اللقب، فإن مفهومه ليس غيره رسول الله وهو رسول الله وهو كفر و لزوم كفر من قال زيد موجود فإن مفهومه ليس غيره موجوداً ظاهراً المعنى أن الكفر بحسب ظاهر العبارة قيل: وقع الإلزام به للدقاق ببغداد وللجدال فيه مجال فإن المفهوم ظني وأضعف من المنطوق، لا سيما المحكم، فيضمحل عند معارضة المنطوق، والمحكمات دلت على رسالة سائر الرسل سلام الله وصلواته عليهم، والقاطع دل على وجود غيره من الله تعالى، وإنما كان هذا جدلاً لأنه يلزم أن يكون كفراً مع قطع النظر عن معارضة أمر آخر، والتزامه شنيع جداً، وأيضاً قد خوطب بهذا القول المشركون أولاً وأمروا بتصديقه، ولم يكن حينئذ المحكمات فحينئذ يكون هذا الكلام تجهيلاً فافهم واستدل
And among them is the concept of title, which is the establishment of a ruling contrary to the articulated ruling for what is beyond the title. What is meant is what encompasses the generic noun. It was held by some Hanbalis and the subtle-minded (al-diqaq) from the Shafi'is and some from the Malikis, but the majority of Hanafis and others deny it. For the majority: firstly, it is a necessary method for expressing the subject by the articulated part, because if not, the articulated part would be disrupted. It is among the greatest benefits and is necessary in every speech. Among the conditions of the concept is the absence of benefits. This applies exactly to the attribute and condition as you have known. And for the majority, secondly: the necessity of disbelief of one who says 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' if the concept of title is established, because its concept is that no one else is the Messenger of Allah, and he is the Messenger of Allah, which is disbelief. And the necessity of disbelief of one who says 'Zayd exists' because its concept is that nothing else exists. Apparently, the meaning is disbelief according to the apparent wording. It is said that this implication was made for the subtle-minded in Baghdad, and there is room for debate. Indeed, the concept is speculative and weaker than the articulated, especially the decisive [texts], so it disappears when opposed by the articulated. The decisive texts indicate the prophethood of other messengers, peace and blessings upon them, and the cut-off evidence indicates the existence of other than Him from Allah. This is merely a dialectical point because it would imply disbelief when considered apart from opposition by another matter, and accepting it is extremely repugnant. Also, this statement was addressed to the polytheists first, and they were commanded to believe him, and at that time there were no decisive texts; thus this speech would be a cause for ignorance. Understand and seek evidence.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of title (mafhum al-laqub), which is the idea that a noun (like a proper name or generic term) implies the negation of the ruling for anything outside it. For example, if one says 'Zayd is standing,' the concept would imply that no one else is standing. The author notes that this concept is accepted by some Hanbalis, a few Shafi'is (called al-diqaq, the subtle ones), and some Malikis, but the majority of Hanafis and others reject it. Two main arguments are presented for the majority: First, the concept of title is a necessary method of expression; if it were not valid, the articulated part would be meaningless. However, the condition for a concept (mafhum) is that it provides no benefit beyond the articulated, but here it does provide benefit (specifying the subject). Second, if the concept of title were valid, it would lead to absurdities: saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' would imply that no one else is a messenger, which contradicts belief in other prophets. Similarly, saying 'Zayd exists' would imply that nothing else exists. This is clearly false. The response to this is that the concept is speculative and weaker than the articulated; when the articulated texts (like the Quran affirming other prophets) are present, the concept is overridden. However, the author notes that this is a dialectical argument (jadal) because if we consider the statement in isolation, it would be blasphemous, but when considered in context of other evidence, it is not. The passage ends by urging the reader to understand and seek further evidence.

Key Terms
مفهوم اللقب (mafhum al-laqub): The implication that a ruling applies exclusively to the named entity and its opposite applies to anything else not named.
الدقاق (al-diqaq): The subtle-minded; a group of Shafi'i scholars who accepted mafhum al-laqub.
مفهوم الصفة (mafhum al-sifah): The concept of an attribute; similar to title but for descriptive phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the majority Hanafi position on mafhum al-laqub?
A) They accept it as a valid concept but restrict it to proper names.
B) They reject it because it leads to absurdities and violates the condition of no benefit.
C) They accept it for generic nouns but not for proper names.
D) They consider it stronger than articulated speech.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-laqub is a disputed usul concept; the Hanafi majority rejects it due to its violation of the 'no benefit' condition and its potential for leading to absurd rulings.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Hanafi Arguments Against Mafhum al-Laqab and the Dialectical Response
Presents the two arguments for rejecting mafhum al-laqub and the dialectical response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main Hanafi arguments against mafhum al-laqub and explain the jadal (dialectical) counter-argument.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-laqub leads to disbelief in prophets and existence of God — an absurdity proving its invalidity.

The Hanafi rejection of mafhum al-laqub rests on two pillars: the condition that a concept must add no benefit, and the absurd consequences of applying it to key creedal statements. This lesson unpacks these arguments and the dialectical response from those who accept it.

Guided Path
1
First Argument: The Benefit Condition
The passage states that a valid concept requires the absence of benefit (i.e., the concept should not convey new information beyond the articulated). In mafhum al-laqub, there is clear benefit in specifying the subject, so it fails this condition.
This argument applies equally to concepts of attribute and condition.
2
Second Argument: The Absurdity of Disbelief
If mafhum al-laqub were accepted, then saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' would imply that no one else is a messenger—which is disbelief. Similarly, 'Zayd exists' would imply nothing else exists—absurd.
The passage calls this a 'necessity of disbelief' (لزوم كفر).
3
The Jadal (Dialectical) Response
The passage acknowledges that when considering the statement in isolation, the implication would indeed be disbelief. However, the concept is speculative (zanni) and weaker than the articulated; stronger decisive texts (muhkamat) override it.
The author notes this is a dialectical argument (jadal) because it isolates the statement from other evidence.
4
Evaluate the Strength of the Arguments
Reflect on why the Hanafi position is preferred: the absurdity is avoided by rejecting the concept, and the condition of no benefit is a sound usul principle.
The passage ends with 'understand and seek evidence,' encouraging critical engagement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المنطوق (al-mantuq): The articulated or explicit meaning of a text.
المحكمات (al-muhkamat): Decisive or clear textual evidence that cannot be overridden.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rejection of mafhum al-laqub is firmly based on two arguments: the condition of no benefit and the absurdity of disbelief; the jadal response does not salvage the concept's validity.

Mantuq and Mafhum

The Condition for Mafhum al-Mukhalafah: Absence of All Benefits
Analyzing the condition for mafhum al-mukhalafah and its relation to qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for mafhum al-mukhalafah and explain why it does not conflict with qiyas.

Core Idea
Mafhum applies only when no benefit (including qiyas) exists; thus qiyas and concept do not overlap.

A common objection is that if mafhum (concept) is valid, qiyas would be invalid because both involve sharing the same ruling. The author responds by clarifying the condition for mafhum al-mukhalafah: it requires the complete absence of any benefit (conformity). Since qiyas provides a benefit, their domains are separate. We will explore this reasoning and the objections raised against the initial answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial objection
The objection states: If mafhum is valid, qiyas would be invalid because both involve sharing the same ruling as the articulated (mantuq). Recognize that this poses a conflict between the two proof types.
The objection assumes mafhum operates in the same domain as qiyas.
2
Understand the initial answer
The initial answer posits that the condition for mafhum is the absence of equality in the common ground (jāmi‘) due to lack of conformity in the ruling. Thus qiyas and mafhum are in different domains.
This answer attempts to separate the domains by restricting mafhum's applicability.
3
Analyze the first objection to the answer
The first objection (from Sharh al-Sharh) argues that if this answer were correct, every qiyas would be a concurrent concept (mafhum muwafaqah), which would make the ruling established by qiyas textual, which is not the case.
This objection challenges the answer's implication that qiyas can be reduced to a linguistic concept.
4
Analyze the second objection
The second objection states that qiyas is based on absolute equality and participation, regardless of the degree of appropriateness. The condition of 'absence of conformity' does not apply because qiyas does not provide textual indication; it is a separate proof.
This objection reinforces that qiyas and concept are fundamentally different types of evidence.
5
Grasp the author's tahqiq (verification)
The author resolves by stating that mafhum al-mukhalafah is built on the complete absence of any benefit (fā’idah), including both manifest conformity (mafhum muwafaqah) and hidden conformity (qiyas). Thus if any qiyas exists that provides conformity, the condition for mafhum is not met, and they do not conflict.
The condition is broadened to 'absence of all benefits', which includes qiyas. This dissolves the objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو كان المفهوم حقاً لكان القياس باطلاً لأنه مشاركة في عين حكم المنطوق، فيضاده المفهوم وأجيب شرطه عدم المساواة في الجامع لانعدام الموافقة في الحكم فلا يجامع المفهوم القياس فليس محل القياس من محال المفهوم فلا يبطل القياس واعترض أولاً كما في شرح الشرح لو صح الجواب لكان كل قياس مفهوماً موافقاً والثابت به ثابتاً بالنص وهو خلف وثانياً كما قيل المعتبر في القياس مطلق المساواة والشركة ولا ينافي ذلك كون المعنى أشد مناسبة للأصل ويكون في الفرع أقل مناسبة، وهذا ليس دلالة النص في شيء، لأن ثبوت الحكم حينئذ ليس جلياً، فهو قياس فحينئذ يجوز اجتماع القياس مع مفهوم المخالف، أقول : التحقيق أن بناء مفهوم المخالفة على عدم الفائدة أصلاً، وذلك بانتفاء الموافقة جلية كانت وهو الموافقة اصطلاحاً أو خفية وهو القياس فإن مطلق الموافقة فائدة، فلا بد من انتفائها، فحيث قالوا : الشرط للمفهوم عدم الموافقة أرادوا أعم لغة أو دلالة أو قياساً فقد ظهر أن محل القياس ليس من محال مفهوم المخالفة وحينئذ الإشكالان يندفعان فافهم وهذا بعينه ما قال في التلويح إن شرط المفهوم انتفاء المشاركة في علة الحكم، فيجب انتفاؤه فلا يبطل به القياس، وهذا غير وافٍ لأن انتفاء القياس لا يكون معلوماً ولا مظنوناً إلا إذا غلب فحص المجتهد ولم يجد، فالمفهوم لا يثبت إلا عند المجتهد بعد نظر أدق، فلا تكون الدلالة لغوية، وإن قيل بانتفاء القياس بالمفهوم لكونه منصوصاً بطل بالكلية وهذه الحجة تبطل سائر أقسام المفهوم، وكنت قد عرضت هذا على أبي مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره فأفاد أن مذهبهم أن المفهوم مدلول للكلام، لكن القياس دليل يعارضه، وهو قوي عن المفهوم فيقدم عليه للتعارض كما يقدم على العام المخصوص، وهذا لا يضر كونه مدلولاً للكلام فافهم فإنه غاية التوجيه وعبارات أكثر معتبراتهم تأبى عنه، فإنهم قالوا : الشرط عدم الفوائد بأسرها سوى المفهوم وعدوا منها الدلالة والقياس فتدبر
If the concept were true, qiyas would be invalid because it is a participation in the very ruling of the articulated, so the concept would oppose it. And it was answered: its condition is the absence of equality in the common ground due to the lack of conformity in the ruling, so the concept does not coexist with qiyas. Thus the domain of qiyas is not the domain of the concept, so qiyas is not invalidated. It was objected: firstly, as in Sharh al-Sharh, if the answer were correct, then every qiyas would be a concurrent concept (mafhum muwafiq), and what is established by it would be established by the text, which is contrary [to reality]. Secondly, as it is said, what is considered in qiyas is absolute equality and participation, and that does not contradict that the meaning is more fitting for the original and less fitting in the branch. This is not textual indication at all, because the establishment of the ruling then is not clear; it is qiyas. Thus it is permissible for qiyas to coexist with the concept of divergent effect. I say: the verification is that the construction of the concept of divergent effect is based on the absence of benefit entirely, and that is by the absence of conformity, whether it is manifest – which is conformity terminologically – or hidden, which is qiyas. For absolute conformity is a benefit, so its absence is necessary. Therefore, when they said: the condition for the concept is the absence of conformity, they meant broadly, whether linguistic, textual indication, or qiyas. Thus it has become clear that the domain of qiyas is not the domain of the concept of divergent effect. Then the two objections are repelled. Understand. This is exactly what is said in al-Talwih: the condition for the concept is the absence of participation in the ‘illah of the ruling, so its absence is necessary, thus qiyas is not invalidated by it. But this is insufficient because the absence of qiyas is not known nor presumed unless the mujtahid's investigation prevails and he does not find [it]. Thus the concept is only established by the mujtahid after more precise consideration, so the indication is not linguistic. And if it is said that the negation of qiyas by the concept is because it is textual, it becomes completely invalid, and this argument invalidates all other types of concept. I had presented this to Abu Matla‘ al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya, may Allah sanctify his secret, and he informed me that their madhhab is that the concept is a meaning (madlul) of the speech, but qiyas is a proof that opposes it, and it is stronger than the concept, so it is given precedence due to conflict, just as it is given precedence over a specified general text. This does not harm its being a meaning of the speech. Understand, for it is the ultimate guidance. However, the expressions of most of their authoritative works reject this, for they said: the condition is the absence of all benefits except the concept, and they count among them textual indication and qiyas. So reflect.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that if concepts (mafhum) are valid, then qiyas would be invalid because both involve sharing the same ruling. The response is that the concept of divergent effect (mafhum al-mukhalafah) requires the absence of any benefit (i.e., the absence of conformity), whereas qiyas provides a benefit by indicating a ruling through common ‘illah. Therefore, they operate in different domains and do not conflict. The author then raises two objections: first, if this were true, every qiyas would be a concurrent concept (mafhum al-muwafaqah), making it textual, which is not the case. Second, qiyas is based on pure equality of ‘illah, not necessarily on a textual indication, so how can the condition of 'absence of conformity' be applied? The author's own investigation (tahqiq) is that the concept of divergent effect is built on the complete absence of benefit, including both manifest conformity (mafhum al-muwafaqah) and hidden conformity (qiyas). Thus, if there is any conformity (even via qiyas), the concept does not hold. This resolves the objections. However, the author notes that the explanation in al-Talwih (by al-Taftazani) is insufficient because the absence of qiyas is not easily determined. Moreover, a more refined view (from Abu Matla‘ al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya) is that the concept is a meaning of speech, but qiyas is a stronger proof that overrides it, like the case of a specified general text. But the author remarks that many reliable works of the Hanafis reject this, insisting that the condition is the absence of all benefits besides the concept itself. The passage ends with an invitation to reflect (fafham, fata dabbar).

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The concept that implies a ruling contrary to the articulated one, based on the absence of conformity (benefit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's tahqiq, what is the condition for mafhum al-mukhalafah to apply?
A) The absence of any qiyas on the matter.
B) The absence of any benefit (conformity) at all, whether linguistic, dalalah, or qiyas.
C) The presence of a clear textual indication.
D) The ruling must be from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The condition for mafhum al-mukhalafah is the complete absence of any benefit, including qiyas, so they do not conflict.

Mantuq and Mafhum
advanced
12 min
Mafhum Mukhalafa and Qiyas: The Condition of Absence of Concurrence
Establishes that mafhum mukhalafa requires absence of qiyas due to conflict in 'illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a mafhum mukhalafa is valid by applying the Hanafi condition of absence of all forms of concurrence, including qiyas.

Core Idea
Mafhum mukhalafa and qiyas cannot coexist when sharing the same 'illa; condition for mafhum is absence of all concurrence.

In Hanafi usul, the concept of opposition (mafhum mukhalafa) is a valid source of law, but it is subject to strict conditions. One critical condition is that there must be no concurrence (muwafaqa) in the ruling, whether that concurrence is explicit (dalala) or hidden (qiyas). This passage explores the dispute regarding the relationship between mafhum and qiyas, and why the Hanafi school holds that qiyas overrides mafhum when they conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether qiyas invalidates mafhum mukhalafa. The initial objection claims that if mafhum were true, qiyas would be false because they share the same ruling.
2
State the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response asserts that the condition for mafhum is the absence of any concurrence (muwafaqa) in the ruling. Since qiyas constitutes hidden concurrence, it blocks mafhum.
Concurrence includes both explicit (dalala) and implicit (qiyas).
3
Analyze the first objection
Objectors argue that if the answer were correct, every qiyas would be a congruent concept (mafhum muwafiq) and thus reduce qiyas to textual proof, which is false.
4
Address the second objection
Another objection states that qiyas considers absolute equality and partnership in the 'illa, but the meaning may be more suitable for the original and less for the branch, so it is not a textual indication. The Hanafi response reaffirms that any concurrence, even less perfect, prevents mafhum.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi tarjih
The passage concludes that qiyas is a stronger proof than mafhum, so when they conflict, qiyas takes precedence. The condition for mafhum is the absence of all benefits (including qiyas) except the mafhum itself.
This is consistent with the view in al-Talwih and the author's teacher.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا الكلام تجهيلاً فافهم واستدل لو كان المفهوم (حقاً لكان القياس باطلاً) لأنه مشاركة في عين حكم المنطوق، فيضاده المفهوم (وأجيب شرطه عدم المساواة) في الجامع لانعدام الموافقة) في الحكم (فلا يجامع) المفهوم (القياس) فليس محل القياس من محال المفهوم فلا يبطل القياس واعترض أولاً كما في شرح الشرح لو صح الجواب (لكان كل قياس مفهوماً) موافقاً (والثابت به ثابتاً بالنص) وهو خلف (وثانياً كما قيل المعتبر في القياس مطلق المساواة) والشركة (ولا ينافي ذلك كون المعنى أشد مناسبة للأصل ويكون في الفرع أقل مناسبة، وهذا ليس دلالة النص في شيء، لأن ثبوت الحكم حينئذ ليس جلياً، فهو قياس (فحينئذ يجوز اجتماع القياس مع مفهوم المخالف، أقول : التحقيق أن بناء) مفهوم (المخالفة على عدم الفائدة أصلاً، وذلك بانتفاء الموافقة جلية كانت وهو الموافقة اصطلاحاً أو خفية وهو القياس) فإن مطلق الموافقة فائدة، فلا بد من انتفائها، فحيث قالوا : الشرط) للمفهوم (عدم الموافقة أرادوا أعم لغة أو دلالة أو قياساً فقد ظهر أن محل القياس ليس من محال مفهوم المخالفة (وحينئذ) الإشكالان يندفعان فافهم وهذا بعينه ما قال في التلويح إن شرط المفهوم انتفاء المشاركة في علة الحكم، فيجب انتفاؤه فلا يبطل به القياس، وهذا غير وافٍ لأن انتفاء القياس لا يكون معلوماً ولا مظنوناً إلا إذا غلب فحص المجتهد ولم يجد، فالمفهوم لا يثبت إلا عند المجتهد بعد نظر أدق، فلا تكون الدلالة لغوية، وإن قيل بانتفاء القياس بالمفهوم لكونه منصوصاً بطل بالكلية وهذه الحجة تبطل سائر أقسام المفهوم، وكنت قد عرضت هذا على أبي مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره فأفاد أن مذهبهم أن المفهوم مدلول للكلام، لكن القياس دليل يعارضه، وهو قوي عن المفهوم فيقدم عليه للتعارض كما يقدم على العام المخصوص، وهذا لا يضر كونه مدلولاً للكلام فافهم فإنه غاية التوجيه وعبارات أكثر معتبراتهم تأبى عنه، فإنهم قالوا : الشرط عدم الفوائد بأسرها سوى المفهوم وعدوا منها الدلالة والقياس فتدبر،
This speech is an insult, so understand and deduce. If the concept (mafhum) were true, then qiyas would be invalid because it shares in the very ruling of the mantuq, contradicting the concept. It was answered: its condition is the absence of equality in the common factor due to lack of concurrence in the ruling, so the concept does not accompany qiyas. Thus the domain of qiyas is not from the domains of the concept, so qiyas is not invalidated. An objection was first raised as in the commentary of the commentary: if the answer were correct, then every qiyas would be a congruent concept, and what is established by it would be established by the text, which is contrary to fact. Secondly, as it was said, the consideration in qiyas is absolute equality and partnership, and this does not conflict with the meaning being more suitable for the original and less suitable for the branch; this is not textual indication in any way because the establishment of the ruling then is not evident; it is qiyas. Then one might say that the conjunction of qiyas with concept of opposition is permissible. I say: the reality is that the construction of the concept of opposition is on the absence of benefit entirely, that is by the absence of concurrence, whether evident – which is concordance terminologically – or hidden – which is qiyas. For absolute concurrence is a benefit, so its absence is necessary. So when they said: the condition for the concept is absence of concurrence, they meant generally whether by language, indication, or qiyas. Thus it became apparent that the domain of qiyas is not from the domains of the concept of opposition, and then the two problems are repelled. Understand. This is exactly what was said in al-Talwih: the condition of the concept is the negation of participation in the 'illa of the ruling, so its negation is necessary, and qiyas is not invalidated by it. But this is insufficient, because the negation of qiyas is not known or conjectured except when the mujtahid's investigation prevails and he does not find it. So the concept is only established for the mujtahid after more precise consideration, so the indication is not linguistic. And if it is said that qiyas is negated by the concept because it is textual, it is invalidated entirely, and this argument invalidates all other types of concept. I had presented this to Abi Mutli' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya (may his soul be sanctified), and he informed that their school is that the concept is a signification of speech, but qiyas is a proof that opposes it, and it is stronger than the concept, so it is given precedence due to conflict, just as it is given precedence over a specific general. This does not harm its being a signification of speech. Understand, for it is the ultimate guidance, but the expressions of most of their reliable books are averse to it, for they said: the condition is the absence of all benefits except the concept, and they counted among them indication and qiyas. So ponder.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the relationship between mafhum mukhalafa (concept of opposition) and qiyas (analogical reasoning). The discussion arises from a matn statement that if mafhum were true, qiyas would be invalid. The commentator explains that the condition for mafhum is the absence of any concurrence (muwafaqa) in the ruling, whether that concurrence is explicit (dalala) or implicit (qiyas). Therefore, when qiyas is applicable, mafhum cannot operate because they share the same 'illa. The text then responds to objections: if qiyas were always a mafhum muwafiq (congruent concept), it would reduce qiyas to textual proof, which is false; but qiyas often involves a lesser suitability than the original, so it is distinct. The commentator resolves by stating that the domain of qiyas is not part of mafhum, so no conflict. He also references al-Talwih and a consultation with a teacher to clarify that mafhum is a dalil (indication) from speech, but qiyas is a stronger proof that overrides it, similar to how a specific proof overrides a general one. The passage ends by noting that many Hanafi scholars consider the condition to be the absence of all other benefits (including qiyas and dalala) for mafhum to be valid.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): A ruling that is understood from the text by implication that applies to cases not mentioned, opposite to the stated ruling.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that extends a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared 'illa.
موافقة (muwafaqa): Concurrence or agreement in the ruling, which when present prevents the application of mafhum mukhalafa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the condition for mafhum mukhalafa to be valid?
A) It must not contradict a general text.
B) There must be no concurrence (muwafaqa) in the ruling, whether by dalala or qiyas.
C) The qiyas must be of a higher strength than the mafhum.
D) The mafhum must be derived from a mutawatir text.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum mukhalafa requires the absence of all forms of concurrence (muwafaqa), including qiyas; if a qiyas shares the same 'illa, it overrides the mafhum.

Mantuq and Mafhum

Mafhum al-Laqab: Hanafi Critique
Presents arguments for and against mafhum al-laqab with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi critique of mafhum al-laqab and explain why apparent understandings from proper nouns are attributed to 'umum or qarina rather than legal implication.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-laqab is not a valid proof; apparent understandings from proper nouns are due to contextual clues or generality.

This passage presents the debate on whether mafhum al-laqab (the implication from a proper noun) is a legitimate source of legal rulings. Proponents argue that when someone says 'My mother is not an adulteress,' the immediate understanding that he accuses his mother of adultery shows that proper nouns can carry an opposite implication. The Hanafi response refutes this by attributing the understanding to contextual clues (qarina) and not to a linguistic principle that would apply to every proper noun. Additionally, the passage examines the Ansar's understanding of the Prophet's statement 'Water, water' and shows that their understanding stemmed from the generality of the definite article, not mafhum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim of mafhum al-laqab proponents
The proponents claim that the immediate understanding from a phrase like 'my mother is not an adulteress' proves that a proper noun implies the opposite ruling for others. They cite that the hadd for qadhf is applied in this case according to Malik and Ahmad.
2
Analyze the Hanafi refutation of the first argument
The Hanafi response argues that the understanding is due to a specific contextual clue (qarina) in that construction, not a general linguistic principle. Moreover, the supposed mafhum would be the affirmation of adultery for someone other than the mother, which is not intended.
3
Examine the second argument from the Ansar's understanding
The Ansar understood from 'Water, water' that ghusl is not required after al-iksal. Proponents say this immediate understanding is a proof for mafhum. The Hanafis respond that the understanding came from the generality of the definite article (al-), meaning 'every ghusl is from semen'.
4
Understand the Hanafi alternative explanation
The meaning is 'all ghusl (due to major ritual impurity) is from semen', so there is no ghusl left for al-iksal. This is similar to Abu Hanifa's understanding of 'the oath is upon the one who denies' as indicating generality. Thus, the understanding is based on 'umum, not mafhum.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The passage shows that the examples cited do not support mafhum al-laqab; instead, they are explained by other well-established usul principles (qarina, 'umum). Therefore, Hanafis reject mafhum al-laqab as an independent proof. The practical consequence: Hanafis do not derive rulings from proper nouns alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثبتو مفهوم اللقب (قالوا: لو قال لخصمه ليست أمي زانية يتبادر منه (نسبته أي نسبة الزنا (إلى أمه، ولذا وجب الحد حد القذف عند الإمامين (مالك) وأحمد (قلنا هذا الانفهام (بالقرينة) الجزئية في هذا التركيب (لا) (باللغة حتى يلزم في كل لقب على أن هذا ليس من المفهوم، فإن مفهوم ثبوت الزنا لما سوى أمه أو أم كل واحد وهو ليس منفهما البتة، قالوا ثانياً : فهم الأنصار رضوان الله عليهم من قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم الماء الماء» عدم وجوب الغسل من الإكسال وهم من أجلة أهل اللسان ففهمهم حجة قلنا : فهمهم من العموم من اللام لأن المعنى كل غسل من المني، فلم يبق غسلاً خارجاً عنه حتى يكون من الإكسال وهذا مثل ما فهم الإمام أبو حنيفة من حديث اليمين على من أنكر عدم اليمين على المدعي، لأن المعنى : كل يمين على من أنكر ، وإنما أوجب الأئمة الأربعة الغسل من الإكسال بقوله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام إذا جلس الرجل بين شعبها الأربع فقد وجب الغسل رواه الشيخان والحديث الأول مخصوص بالاحتلام على ما روى خصوص المستفاد وجهد الترمذي عن ابن عباس .
Those who affirm mafhum al-laqab said: if someone says to his opponent 'My mother is not an adulteress', there is an immediate understanding that he is attributing adultery to his mother, and therefore the hadd punishment for qadhf applies according to the two Imams Malik and Ahmad. We say: this understanding is due to a specific contextual clue in this construction, not due to linguistic principle that would apply to every laqab. Moreover, this is not a mafhum because the mafhum would be the affirmation of adultery for someone other than his mother, or for every mother, which is not the case at all. They said secondly: The Ansar (may Allah be pleased with them) understood from his statement (peace be upon him) 'Water, water' the non-obligation of ghusl from al-iksal (touching?), and they are among the most proficient in language, so their understanding is a proof. We say: their understanding was from generality of the lam, because the meaning is 'Every ghusl is from semen', so no ghusl remained outside it to be from al-iksal. This is similar to what Imam Abu Hanifa understood from the hadith 'The oath is upon the one who denies', that there is no oath upon the claimant, because the meaning is 'Every oath is upon the one who denies'. And the four Imams obligated ghusl from al-iksal by his statement (peace be upon him) 'When the man sits between her four limbs, ghusl becomes obligatory' narrated by al-Shaykhayn, and the first hadith is specific to wet dream according to what was narrated by al-Tirmidhi from Ibn Abbas.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding mafhum al-laqab (concept of the proper noun). Proponents argue that when someone says 'my mother is not an adulteress', the listener immediately understands that the speaker is accusing his mother of adultery, and thus the hadd of qadhf applies according to Malik and Ahmad. The Hanafi response is that this understanding comes from a contextual clue (qarina) in this specific phrase, not from linguistic principle, so it does not establish a general rule for every laqab (proper noun). Moreover, this is not a true mafhum because the opposite would be that adultery is affirmed for someone other than his mother, which is not intended. The second argument: the Ansar understood from the Prophet's statement 'Water, water' that ghusl is not required from al-iksal (apparently a type of sexual activity). But the Hanafi refutation explains that the Ansar's understanding was based on the generality of the definite article (al-), meaning 'all ghusl is from semen', so no ghusl remains for al-iksal. Similarly, Imam Abu Hanifa understood from 'the oath is on the one who denies' that there is no oath on the claimant, again due to 'umum. Finally, the passage notes that the four Imams actually obligated ghusl from al-iksal based on another hadith, and the first hadith is restricted to wet dream according to a narration from Tirmidhi. So the proponents' arguments are refuted, supporting the Hanafi rejection of mafhum al-laqab as an independent proof.

Key Terms
مفهوم اللقب (mafhum al-laqab): The implication from a proper noun (laqab) that those not bearing that noun have the opposite ruling.
قرينة (qarina): Contextual clue that determines the intended meaning, as opposed to linguistic designation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi scholar explain the Ansar's understanding from the Prophet's statement 'Water, water'?
A) They understood it as a mafhum al-laqab.
B) They understood it from the generality of the definite article (al-), meaning 'all ghusl is from semen'.
C) They understood it from a contextual clue specific to that situation.
D) They did not actually understand it that way; it is a false narration.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-laqab is not a valid proof in Hanafi usul; apparent understandings from proper nouns are explained by qarina or 'umum.
